# FreeITSM Changelog

This file tracks all fixes, improvements, and features for website updates.
Items are logged here and then published to the updates page at freeitsm.co.uk/updates.html.

Each entry has a unique ID (3-digit, sequential) used as `data-id` on the website update items.
When publishing to the website, move entries from **Unpublished** to the **Published** section.

---

## Unpublished



| ID  | Module            | Type        | Description |
|-----|-------------------|-------------|-------------|
| 595 | Messaging         | Improvement | **Meta WhatsApp Cloud API production-readiness.** Bumped the Graph API version from the ageing `v19.0` to `v21.0` (Meta deprecates a version ~2 years after release), and made it overridable per channel without a code change via an optional `graph_version` key in the channel credentials. Reviewed the Meta provider's webhook verification (GET `hub.challenge` handshake + `X-Hub-Signature-256` HMAC), inbound parsing (correctly ignores status-update webhooks) and send path against the live API shape. Documented the full Meta Cloud API setup, plus **Cloudflare Tunnel** as the recommended way for firewalled self-hosters to receive inbound WhatsApp (a stable, reboot-surviving public hostname &mdash; ngrok is now framed as dev-only). |
| 594 | Messaging         | Fix         | **Encrypt all channel secrets at rest, not just provider credentials.** The provider credentials blob (Twilio Account SID/Auth Token, Meta access token/app secret) was already AES-256-GCM encrypted, but the `verify_token` and `relay_secret` columns were stored in plaintext. Both are now encrypted with the same `encryptValue()` (decrypted on load; migration-safe so any pre-existing plaintext still reads). On edit these behave as write-only fields (blank keeps the stored value). Verified: no plaintext secret remains in `messaging_channels`. |
| 593 | Messaging         | Fix         | **Outbound WhatsApp replies failed with "SSL certificate problem" on installs without a CA bundle.** The messaging provider's cURL helper didn't set `CURLOPT_SSL_VERIFYPEER`, so it defaulted to strict verification and failed on dev boxes (e.g. WAMP) that lack a `cacert.pem` — unlike every other outbound HTTPS call in the app. Now `MessagingProvider::httpRequest()` honours the app-wide `SSL_VERIFY_PEER` config flag (and sets `CURLOPT_SSL_VERIFYHOST` to match), consistent with the email/AI/vCenter cURL calls. |
| 592 | Messaging         | Improvement | **Set a public base URL for webhook addresses, so the displayed webhook URL is copy-paste-ready.** Previously the Messaging settings page showed each channel's webhook URL using whatever address you were browsing from (usually `localhost`), forcing self-hosters to hand-edit it before pasting into Twilio/Meta. Now there's a **Public base URL** field at the top of **Tickets → Settings → Messaging**: set your public domain (or your `ngrok` address while testing) once and every channel's webhook URL is rebuilt against it. Stored as `system_settings` `messaging_public_base_url` (origin only — scheme/host/port; any path is stripped); blank falls back to the request-derived address (previous behaviour). New endpoint `save_base_url.php`; `get_channels.php` uses the setting when present and returns it. |
| 591 | Messaging         | Feature     | **WhatsApp channel — customers can chat with an analyst, and the conversation becomes a ticket.** A new **Messaging** channel sits alongside email: an inbound WhatsApp message creates (or threads into an open) ticket tagged with the new **WhatsApp** origin, and analysts reply straight from the reading pane via an inline composer. Built on a provider abstraction (`includes/messaging/` — `MessagingProvider` + `TwilioProvider` + `MetaCloudProvider`) so **Twilio** (recommended first build, has a sandbox) and **Meta WhatsApp Cloud API** are interchangeable. Inbound arrives at a public webhook (`api/messaging/webhook.php?channel=<id>`), verified by the provider signature (**direct** mode) or a shared secret (**relay** mode) — the configurable ingress choice. Conversations reuse the existing email "membrane": same `emails` table (new `channel` + `channel_id` columns), same reading-pane thread, same multi-tenancy isolation (new `resolveTicketTenantForChannel()` mirrors email routing: pinned channel → company, else exact sender-number map → company, else triage). The provider **24-hour service window** is first-class: `tickets.last_inbound_at` drives the composer, which blocks free-text replies once the window closes (templates come later). Two **AI** helpers in v1: summarise the conversation into a ticket note, and draft a suggested reply. Managed under **Tickets → Settings → Messaging** (add/edit/delete channels; each row shows the webhook URL to paste into the provider). New tables `messaging_channels` + `tenant_channel_senders` (+ `freeitsm.sql`/`db_verify`); `inbox.js`/`inbox.css` updated for the composer. Self-hosted/local testing uses a tunnel (e.g. `ngrok http 80`) since providers can only reach a public HTTPS URL. ⚠️ **After updating, run Database Verify** so the new tables/columns exist. |
| 590 | Tickets           | Feature     | **Trash with restore — deleting a ticket is no longer permanent.** Until now, deleting a ticket hard-deleted it and all its emails/attachments/notes with no undo. Now **Delete** is **"Move to trash"** (a soft-delete: sets `deleted_datetime`/`deleted_by`, removes nothing), and a new **Trash** folder (pinned to the bottom of the inbox folder list, with a count) shows trashed tickets with per-row **↩ Restore** and **✕ Delete forever** buttons. Permanent deletion (the old irreversible removal + attachment-file cleanup) now lives behind "Delete forever" and only acts on a ticket already in the trash. Trashed tickets are hidden from **everywhere else** — the inbox list, all folder/department/analyst counts, search, the calendar, per-user ticket counts, dashboard widgets, and the System Topology/Orphaned-tickets screens (a `deleted_datetime IS NULL` filter was added to all of them) — and shown **only** in the Trash folder (`get_emails.php?trashed=1`). Schema: `tickets.deleted_datetime` + `deleted_by` (`freeitsm.sql` + `db_verify`). New endpoints `restore_ticket.php` and `permanently_delete_ticket.php`; `delete_ticket.php` now soft-deletes; `get_ticket_counts.php` returns `trash_count`. Every trash/restore writes a `ticket_audit` entry. The **SLA breach cron** skips trashed tickets (no notifications fire on a deleted ticket). Opening a trashed ticket in the reading pane shows a **"This ticket is in the trash"** banner with Restore / Delete-forever and greys out the normal workflow actions until it's restored (`get_email_detail` now returns `deleted_datetime`). **Three ways to trash:** the reading-pane Delete button, **drag a ticket onto the Trash folder**, or **right-click a ticket → Move to trash**. **Right-click the Trash folder → Empty trash** permanently purges all trashed tickets in the active company (confirm + count toast; new `empty_trash.php`). `inbox.js` cache-buster v=35. ⚠️ **After updating, run Database Verify** so the new columns exist. |
| 589 | System            | Feature     | **New System → Orphaned tickets screen — find and rehome tickets stuck in a deleted department.** A ticket whose `department_id` points at a department that no longer exists is invisible to every team-filtered queue (it's neither "no department" nor in anyone's departments), so it silently disappears from the inbox — exactly the kind of thing the Topology view surfaced (e.g. 23 demo tickets pointing at dropped department ids). The new screen lists every such ticket (ticket #, subject, company at N>1, requester, status, the dead department id) and lets you **reassign** them to a real department — or to "No department" — one at a time or in bulk (select-all + assign). New endpoints `api/system/get_orphaned_tickets.php` (lists orphans + valid departments) and `api/system/assign_ticket_department.php` (validates the target, updates `tickets.department_id`, writes a `ticket_audit` entry per ticket). New System landing card (searchable — *orphaned / stuck / deleted department / reassign*). Shows a clean "✅ none" state when everything resolves. |
| 588 | System            | Feature     | **New System → Topology view — see how everything fits together.** A read-only, collapsible **company-rooted tree** that pulls the whole configuration into one screen: each company with its **mailboxes** (pinned, with signed-in/active badges), **domains** & specific senders, **sign-in providers**, **analysts with access**, **requester** count (by email domain) and **ticket** totals — plus a **Global / shared** node for things that serve every company (shared mailboxes, global SSO providers, all-access analysts). Honours the model's many-to-many shape rather than faking a strict hierarchy (shared mailboxes are noted under each company but listed once under Global; cross-company access is shown via the all-access node). **Health hints** tie into the recent work: a company with no sendable mailbox is flagged, and mailboxes show a *not signed in* badge. Includes a totals bar, company filter, expand/collapse-all, and deep-links out to the relevant editors (Companies, Single Sign-On, Analyst settings). New aggregation endpoint `api/system/get_topology.php`; new System landing card (searchable — *map / overview / relationships / structure*). *v1 is read-only with requester counts (not yet the lazy-loaded requester list); refinements to follow.* |
| 587 | Tickets           | Fix         | **Reply modal: To/Cc no longer autocomplete, and now sit side by side.** Added `autocomplete="off"` to the To and Cc inputs in the reply/forward modal (browsers were offering saved-value dropdowns over them), and laid them out on a single two-column row instead of stacked — tidier and matches the New Ticket modal's requester name/email row. |
| 586 | System            | Improvement | **SSO providers list now shows which company each provider belongs to.** On a multi-company install, the System → Single Sign-On providers table gains a **Company** column showing the client company a provider is pinned to, or **Global** for an MSP-internal/all-companies provider — so it's obvious at a glance why (e.g.) a client's IdP doesn't appear on the analyst login. `get_sso_providers.php` now returns each provider's `tenant_name` (LEFT JOIN tenants). The column is hidden at N=1 (single company), consistent with the rest of multi-tenancy. The **issuer** column already truncates with an ellipsis and shows the full issuer URL on hover (title tooltip). |
| 585 | Tickets           | Fix         | **Manually-created tickets can now send replies — pick the mailbox when you raise one.** A ticket's send-from mailbox is resolved via its emails' `mailbox_id`, but manual ticket creation left that NULL, so replying to a "raise on behalf of someone" ticket failed with *"Could not determine mailbox for this ticket."* The **New Ticket** modal now has a **"Send replies from"** dropdown, populated (via new `api/tickets/get_sendable_mailboxes.php`) with the mailboxes relevant to the company the ticket is being raised in — its **pinned** mailbox(es) **plus shared-intake** ones — and only those that are **active and signed-in**, so the choice can actually send. `create_ticket.php` stamps the chosen `mailbox_id` on the initial email. **Multi-tenant safe:** the list is scoped to the analyst's active company (a read-only company label is shown next to the field at N>1 so it's clear which company's mailboxes these are), and the server **rejects** a mailbox that doesn't belong to that company (can't attach another company's pinned mailbox). **N=1 unaffected** — it simply lists all active, signed-in mailboxes. If there are no sendable mailboxes the ticket can still be created (the field says so), it just can't email a reply yet. `inbox.js` cache-buster bumped to v=32. *(Known follow-ups logged: a soft "this looks like a different company" warning on the requester email, and a "move ticket to another company" action — since a mis-filed ticket is currently sticky.)* |
| 584 | System            | Feature     | **New debug tool D004 — Local login check (password / hash).** Diagnoses why a username/email + password sign-in fails, built for the common *"I bulk-imported accounts with password hashes but they can't log in"* support case. Pick the account type (analyst / self-service user), enter the username/email, and **optionally** the password. It runs **hash forensics** — detects bcrypt/argon vs an imported **MD5 / SHA-1 / SHA-256 / phpass / Django / LDAP** hash that PHP's `password_verify()` can never read (so login always fails until the password is re-set and re-hashed with bcrypt) — flags whitespace/length anomalies, checks account-state blockers (inactive, locked, password expired, **SSO-pinned** so local is disabled, TOTP required, active IP bans), and — for MFA users — whether the **encryption key** can actually decrypt this account's TOTP secret (a wrong/missing key fails login *after* a correct password, at the 6-digit step; password hashes themselves aren't encrypted, so the key never affects password-only login). Prints a plain-English verdict + fix. If you supply the password it runs `password_verify()` and, when that fails on a raw digest, **pinpoints the wrong-hash-type import** by testing whether the stored hash is e.g. `MD5(password)` — naming the exact root cause. **Safe to share:** it's **POST-only** (the new multi-field debug-tools input framework — text/password/select fields — keeps the password out of the URL/logs), the password is never echoed, and the stored hash is never printed (only its format/cost/length). Backend `api/system/debug-tools/D004_local_login.php`; registry entry + `d004/` page. (Verified live by reproducing the MD5-import case — it correctly reported "the stored hash EQUALS MD5(the supplied password)".) |
| 583 | System            | Feature     | **New debug tool D003 — Self-Service SSO check (by email).** Type a requester's email, click Run, and it traces the whole self-service single-sign-on path end to end and prints a verdict with any blockers: schema readiness (users / user_sso_identities / auth_providers / system_settings + the multi-tenant routing tables + key constraints), global SSO config (`sso_enabled`, `local_login_enabled`, global-vs-company-owned provider counts), single- vs multi-tenant mode, how the email maps to a company (exact sender override → domain mapping → freemail detection), the user account state (exists / passwordless / TOTP / which provider it's pinned to / linked identities), the **predicted login outcome** — local / sso / choose — mirroring the real `resolve_login.php`, **provider health with a live, secret-free OIDC discovery test** (issuer match + authorization/token/jwks/end-session endpoints reachable, *without* using the client secret), and the exact **redirect URI** to register in the IdP. **Read-only and safe to share** — client secrets, TOTP secrets and password hashes are reported only as present/absent, the IdP subject is masked, and because the report is designed to be copy-pasted to support, the **identifiers are partially masked too** (client IDs and tenant GUIDs show first/last chars only — enough to eyeball-verify, not the full value; the issuer-match and endpoint-reachability checks still run on the real values). Backend script `api/system/debug-tools/D003_selfservice_sso.php`; slots into the new debug-tools registry as `d003/`. (Verified live against pinned / picker / freemail emails — it correctly flagged an unreachable IdP discovery as a blocker.) |
| 582 | System            | Improvement | **Debug tools restructured: searchable catalogue + a page per tool.** Ahead of more diagnostics being added, the Debug Tools area now works like the System landing — a **registry** (`system/debug-tools/includes/tools.php`) drives a grid of cards (ID badge, icon, category, short description) that **filters live on every keypress**, and each card opens that tool on **its own page** at `system/debug-tools/<slug>/index.php` (e.g. `d001/`, `d002/`) instead of everything being stacked inline on one screen. A per-tool page is just two lines — set the slug and include the shared `includes/tool-page.php` renderer (which holds the detail layout + Run/Copy logic); the diagnostic's metadata (when to run, checks, runtime, side-effects, any input) lives in the registry. The backend diagnostic scripts (`api/system/debug-tools/Dnnn_*.php`) are unchanged. **Adding a tool is now: a registry entry + a two-line page + the API script.** No behaviour change to D001/D002 themselves; D002 keeps its destructive-delete warning. |
| 581 | System            | Feature     | **In-app help for every System area.** Added a help section at `system/help/` — a landing page (`system/help/index.php`) with a card per System area (driven by the same `system/includes/areas.php` registry as the System landing, so the two stay in step), plus a dedicated, step-by-step help page for each area: encryption, modules, database verification, module colours, branding, security, preferences, demo data, debug tools, companies, email routing test, and a flagship **Single Sign-On** guide. The SSO page spells out the two paths super-clearly — **single-company** (one IdP, three steps) vs **multi-company / MSP** (per-client domains + company-owned providers, the email-first router, the 0/1/2+ picker, what to collect from each client, and break-glass safety). All pages share one indigo layout (`_init`/`_top`/`_bottom`) with a left-nav + scroll-spy, matching the existing module help style; written in plain English (System is English-only). **Discoverability:** the System landing gains a distinct **Help & guides** card (rendered directly, so it doesn't recurse onto the help landing) that's also searchable, and the System → **Companies** page carries a banner — *“Setting up single sign-on for the self-service portal? Click here for the step-by-step guide”* — linking straight to the SSO help. |
| 580 | Self-Service      | Feature     | **Multi-tenant SSO on the self-service portal — route each client company's requesters to their own identity provider.** Builds on #579. A provider can now be **owned by a client company** (`auth_providers.tenant_id`; NULL = global/MSP-internal). On a multi-tenant install the portal login becomes **email-first only** (no provider buttons up front — they'd leak every client's IdP): you type your email, and a new resolver path maps your **email domain → company → that company's enabled IdP(s)** (reusing the existing `tenant_domains`/`tenant_sender_addresses` routing via a new `resolveTenantIdForAddress()` helper). The company may have **0 IdPs** (→ local password), **1** (→ straight through), or **2+** (→ a **tenant-scoped picker** — "Choose how to sign in" — for a company mid-migration between, say, Entra and Okta). A returning requester is still routed instantly by their per-user pin (`users.auth_provider_id` from #579), so the picker is a once-only first-login step. The SSO admin (System → Single Sign-On) gains a **Company** dropdown per provider (shown only when N>1) to set the owner; `get/save_sso_provider` carry `tenant_id`. The **analyst** login is now scoped to global providers only, so client IdPs never appear there. **Invisible at N=1** — single-company installs keep the exact #579 behaviour (buttons up front), gated on `isMultiTenant()`. *Note: this routes per company using each provider's own credentials (the working handshake); the credential-free "MSP multi-tenant app + consent" onboarding is a further layer, still design-only.* |
| 579 | Self-Service      | Feature     | **SSO on the self-service portal — sign in with your identity provider, not just a password.** The requester portal only ever had email + password; SSO existed for analysts but never for self-service. The portal login page now gets the same **email-first router** as the analyst login (type your email → routed to your provider automatically), plus **provider buttons** and a **local-account break-glass** — and turning *Allow local login* off / `?local=1` behave identically. Under the hood the existing OIDC flow is made **portal-aware**: `oidc_login.php`/`oidc_callback.php`/`resolve_login.php` carry a `portal=self-service` flag, and the one IdP callback resolves against the requester `users` table (not `analysts`), sets the self-service session, and lands in the portal. New `user_sso_identities` table + `users.auth_provider_id` mirror the analyst SSO tables one layer down (`db_verify`/`freeitsm.sql` + FKs/unique idempotent). Because requesters self-onboard, a requester matched by **verified email** who is unassigned is **auto-claimed** onto the provider on first sign-in (analysts, being privileged, still require explicit enrolment), and the provider's *auto-create* toggle JIT-creates brand-new requesters. Self-service **logout** now also ends the IdP session (single logout). Analysts and requesters stay separate identity spaces, so the same email resolves independently per portal. **No change at N=1 with SSO off** — the portal still shows the plain email/password form. *(This is the single-IdP-per-org model; the MSP multi-tenant-app SSO model is captured separately as a design doc.)* |
| 578 | Tickets           | Fix         | **Removed the flicker when clicking between tickets.** Two causes: (1) selecting a ticket immediately blanked the reading pane to a loading spinner *before* fetching the new one, so switching tickets flashed Ticket A → spinner → Ticket B; now the current ticket stays on screen during the (usually instant) fetch and is swapped straight out, with the spinner only shown on first open or if the fetch actually takes >250ms. (2) every click rebuilt the entire email list just to move the selected-row highlight, which also re-fired the batch SLA fetch and made the SLA pills flash off and back on; the highlight now moves via a lightweight class toggle (`data-email-id` on each row) with no list rebuild and no redundant SLA refetch. `inbox.js` cache-buster bumped to v=31. |
| 577 | Tickets           | Improvement | **Right-click menu: set department and type without opening the ticket.** The email-row context menu already had Set status, Set priority and Assign to; added **Set department** and **Set type** submenus alongside them. Each lists the same options as the in-panel dropdowns (departments filtered to the analyst's teams; active ticket types), with a "(no department)"/"(no type)" clear row since both are nullable, and a tick against the current value when right-clicking the ticket open in the reading pane. Picking one saves via the existing `assign_ticket.php` (`department_id` / `ticket_type_id`), writes an audit-trail entry, keeps the open ticket's toolbar in sync, and refreshes the list (department also refreshes folder counts since the inbox can be grouped by department). Bumped the `inbox.js` cache-buster to v=30. |
| 576 | System            | Improvement | **System admin: searchable card navigation, navbar buttons removed.** The System area kept a row of header nav buttons that duplicated the landing-page cards — but it had already outgrown them (only 9 of 13 areas fit; SSO, Companies and Email-routing-test were missing entirely). The navbar buttons are gone; the landing-page cards are now the single source of navigation, and the header "System" title links back to the landing from any sub-page. Added a **search box** on the landing page that filters the cards live by title, description, and hidden keyword synonyms — so searching *oidc*, *saml* or *idp* finds the **Single Sign-On** card even though those words aren't in its title. Cards and search are both driven from one new registry (`system/includes/areas.php`: url, icon, title/desc/keyword i18n keys, optional N>1 visibility) instead of hardcoded markup, killing the card/navbar duplication. Fully i18n — keywords are translation keys (English synonyms wired, other locales fall back per-key until translated) and the search also matches the on-screen translated text, so it works in any language. |
| 575 | System            | Improvement | **Login: local account sign-in now opens in its own modal.** When SSO is the leading sign-in method, clicking "Sign in with a local account" (or falling back to local from the email-first router) previously appended the username/password fields onto the page below the SSO options. They now open in a dedicated centred modal — closable by the ×, clicking the backdrop, or Escape — keeping the SSO-first page clean. A failed local login (or the `?local=1` break-glass) re-opens the modal automatically with the error inside it. No change to single-company / no-SSO installs, where the local form still shows inline. |
| 574 | Tickets           | Feature     | **Multi-tenancy: control which companies an analyst can access (the admin UI for the isolation that was already enforced).** The Phase 1.5 isolation gated everything on an analyst's "accessible companies" — but there was no way to actually *set* that (every analyst defaulted to all-access). The Tickets → Settings → Analysts add/edit dialog now has an **"Access all companies"** toggle; switch it off and tick exactly which companies the analyst may work in. The analyst list flags restricted analysts with a small "N companies" chip. This flows straight into the existing enforcement: a restricted analyst's **company switcher** only shows their companies, their ticket lists/searches/dashboards scope to those, and the by-id guards (`analystCanAccessTicket`) deny everything else. New analysts default to all-access (matches the install default and the "generalist MSP" case). `get_analysts` returns each analyst's `can_access_all_tenants` + granted company ids; `save_analyst` persists them to `analyst_tenant_access`. **Entirely hidden on a single-company install** (the control only appears once a second company exists), so nothing changes at N=1. Completes the account-aligned-MSP access story (design §8). |
| 573 | Tickets           | Improvement | **Documented the multi-company data isolation — in-app help + wiki.** Added a high-level "Each company's tickets stay private" note to the Tickets help "Companies" section (shown only on a multi-company install), and a detailed **Multi-Tenancy-Isolation** wiki page covering the isolation model (the `ticketTenantFilter` list scope + the `analystCanAccessTicket` by-id access check), the cross-company IDOR risk being closed, and the three-sweep hardening audit (what each pass found — including a cross-company delete and an attachment-content read — and how each was fixed), plus the deferred cross-module reads. |
| 572 | Tickets           | Fix         | **Multi-tenancy (Phase 1.5): close the remaining cross-company isolation gaps so multi-company use is actually safe.** Audits + endpoint sweeps found older ticket endpoints that weren't tenant-scoped (harmless at N=1, but a cross-company leak once a second company exists). All now fixed, all no-ops at N=1: **List reads** scoped via `ticketTenantFilter()` (active company) — `search_tickets`, `get_user_tickets` (also upholds the §9 "analysts don't see a requester's other-company tickets" guardrail), `get_scheduled_tickets`, all ~15 `get_ticket_widget_data` dashboard aggregates, and the per-user ticket count in `get_users`. **Detail / child-data reads by id** gated on a new `analystCanAccessTicket()` helper (a ticket is reachable only if its company is in the analyst's accessible set; otherwise "not found") — `get_email_detail`, `get_ticket_thread`, `get_notes`, `get_ticket_attachments`, `get_ticket_audit`, `get_ticket_cmdb_objects`, `get_time_entries`. **Mutations by id** likewise gated — `assign_ticket`, `update_ticket_owner`, `send_email`, `ai_cleanup_reply`, `save_ticket_cmdb_object`, `delete_ticket_cmdb_object`, `delete_ticket` (was a cross-company *delete*), `schedule_ticket`, `save_note`, `save_time_entry`, `log_ticket_audit`. Also gated: **attachment serving** (`get_attachment` — was a cross-company file-content leak — resolved via email→ticket; `debug_get_attachment`), **per-ticket SLA** (`get_ticket_sla`, `get_tickets_sla_batch` — skips inaccessible ids), and **`request_csat`** (can't trigger a survey email for another company's ticket). **Triage write-auth** — `resolve_triage` won't file a ticket into a company the analyst can't access. New helper `analystCanAccessTicket()` in `includes/tenancy.php`. Completes the ticket-layer isolation; a real multi-company go-live is now safe. |
| 571 | Tickets           | Feature     | **Multi-tenancy: per-company ticket origins + documented which settings are/aren't customisable per company.** Applied the #570 add+hide model to **ticket origins** (the clean copy of ticket types): in a client company's context the Settings → Ticket origins tab splits into the company's own origins (add/edit/delete) and the shared defaults it inherits (per-company Hide/Show eye toggle, in-use guarded); the ticket form shows each company its resolved list. New endpoint `set_ticket_origin_hidden.php`; `get/save/delete_ticket_origin.php` context-aware; `ticket_origins.tenant_id` + FK (`db_verify`/`freeitsm.sql`). **Also documented the rationale**: the Tickets help "Companies" section and the **Multi-Tenancy-Settings** wiki page now spell out what's tailored per company (types, origins, categories, SLAs) vs deliberately shared (statuses & priorities — for cross-company reporting + the SLA axis; teams, rota, mailboxes — the MSP's own operation), with the *why* for each. Invisible at N=1. |
| 570 | Tickets           | Feature     | **Multi-tenancy: per-company ticket types (the first per-company setting — add+hide model, design §7).** Ticket types are now a **global default that each company can tailor**. Working in a client company's context, the Tickets → Settings → Ticket types tab splits into two groups: **that company's own types** (add / edit / delete) and the **shared defaults it inherits**, each with a per-company **Hide / Show** toggle — so a client can drop a default it doesn't use or add one only it needs, without affecting anyone else. The shared defaults themselves are still managed from the MSP/Default company (and at N=1 the tab is exactly as before — one flat list). Routing is enforced server-side: a new type belongs to the active company; you can only edit/delete your own; globals are hidden (reversibly — the row is never deleted, so history still resolves) not edited; and **hiding/deleting is blocked while open tickets in that company use the type** (the in-use guard). The ticket form now shows each company its resolved list (its own + non-hidden defaults) automatically. New endpoint `set_ticket_type_hidden.php`; `get/save/delete_ticket_type.php` made context-aware; `ticket_types` name-uniqueness widened to per-company (`db_verify`/`freeitsm.sql`). Built on the #569 `getTenantConfigRows()` + `tenant_config_hidden` foundation; reference implementation for rolling the same pattern to origins, departments and SLAs. Invisible at N=1. |

| 567 | System            | Feature     | **Multi-tenancy: route an individual sender address to a company ("specific senders").** Shared-intake routing matches on the sender's *domain*, which can't separate people on public providers (two clients both on `gmail.com`) — so a freelancer or micro-client emailing from a personal address used to land in triage every time. You can now map an **exact address** (e.g. `jane@gmail.com`) to a company, checked **before** the domain (most-specific-wins), so that one person's mail reaches the right company automatically while everyone else on `gmail.com` still triages. Managed two ways: a **Specific senders** list in the System → Companies editor (the address-level twin of Email domains), and a one-click **"Always file mail from _X_ here"** option when filing a public-provider ticket from the **triage** queue — which sweeps that address's other queued mail and auto-routes its future mail, exactly like domain mapping but freemail-safe. Pinned mailboxes are unaffected (they ignore the sender). Invisible at N=1. |

| 557 | Tickets           | Feature     | **Multi-tenancy (Phase 2): inbound email now routes to a company.** New emails that open a ticket are filed to the right company following the design's ordered rule, via a single new `resolveTicketTenantForEmail()` choke-point in `includes/tenancy.php`: a reply to an existing ticket inherits that ticket's company (unchanged); otherwise a **pinned** mailbox (one assigned to a company) sends its mail to that company and the sender is ignored; a **shared-intake** mailbox (no company) routes by the **sender's domain** matched against each company's registered domains (`tenant_domains`); anything unmatched (including freemail like gmail.com, which is never registered) goes to **triage** — left un-companied so it surfaces under Default until an analyst files it, so nothing is ever lost. | 543 | Tickets           | Improvement | **Google mailbox OAuth hardening — community contribution (PR #23, thanks to @abdulaziz-git).** Builds on #542. (1) All six *encrypted* `target_mailboxes` columns (`azure_tenant_id`, `azure_client_id`, `azure_client_secret`, `oauth_redirect_uri`, `imap_server`, `target_mailbox`) are now `TEXT` rather than fixed-width `VARCHAR`, removing the whole class of "AES-GCM ciphertext is longer than the column" truncation bug for every field, not just the client ID; the db_verify migration widens any non-`TEXT` column on existing installs. (2) `save_mailbox.php` now validates the OAuth redirect URI server-side per provider — a Google mailbox must point at `google_oauth_callback.php` and a Microsoft mailbox at `oauth_callback.php` — so you can't accidentally save a Google mailbox aimed at the Microsoft callback (which would break state parsing). | 542 | Tickets           | Fix         | **Google (Gmail) mailbox setup no longer corrupts itself, taking the whole mailbox list down with it.** The `target_mailboxes.azure_client_id`/`azure_tenant_id` columns were `VARCHAR(100)`, sized for Azure GUIDs (which encrypt to ~92 chars). A Google OAuth client ID is ~72 chars and encrypts to ~140, so MySQL **silently truncated** it on save; the truncated ciphertext then failed AES-GCM decryption ("Decryption failed — data may be corrupted or wrong key"). Because `get_mailboxes.php` decrypted every row up-front, that one bad row made the *entire* mailbox list return an error and appear empty. Fixed three ways: widened both columns to `VARCHAR(255)` in `freeitsm.sql`; added an idempotent `ALTER … MODIFY` in `db_verify` so existing installs are repaired on the next Database Verify (the `$schema` loop only adds missing columns, never widens them); and hardened `get_mailboxes.php` so a single undecryptable row is flagged (`decrypt_error`) instead of blanking the whole list. Re-enter the Client ID after upgrading. |
| 541 | System            | Feature     | **Database Verify: one-click "Fix" for orphaned rows that block a foreign key.** When a ticket-child FK can't be added because orphaned rows exist, the result row now explains it in plain English (e.g. "Found 1 email attachment(s) whose email has been deleted but the attachment rows were left behind…") and shows a **Fix** button. Clicking it (after a confirm) calls a strictly-whitelisted endpoint (`api/system/fix_orphans.php`) that deletes only the rows whose parent is genuinely missing — and, for attachments, removes the now-orphaned files from disk — then automatically re-runs verification so the FK adds cleanly. db_verify itself still never deletes anything; the deletion only happens when the admin clicks Fix. |
| 540 | System            | Feature     | **New debug tool: "Delete Ticket (with full SQL trace)" (D002).** A new diagnostic on System → Debug Tools for the case where a ticket won't delete. The card now supports a **text input** (diagnostics can declare an `input` whose value is passed to the report) — enter the ticket reference and it resolves the ticket, audits every table the delete touches (existence, key columns, every foreign key and its `ON DELETE` rule), **pinpoints the `fk_email_attachments_email` constraint (present? blocking?) and lists the exact email ids + attachment ids / filenames / paths that trigger the error**, counts the child rows that will be removed, then runs the delete inside a transaction echoing **every** SQL statement, its parameters and rows affected, COMMITs, verifies nothing is left behind, and removes the orphaned attachment files. Destructive on success; rolls back on any error. |
| 539 | System            | Improvement | **db_verify now adds the ticket-child foreign keys so upgraded installs match a fresh one.** `email_attachments→emails`, `ticket_notes/ticket_audit/ticket_time_entries→tickets` exist in `freeitsm.sql` but were never added by `db_verify` (its `$schema` only builds columns + PK), so databases grown via Database Verify silently lacked them. Added them to the post-schema FK section (no cascade — `delete_ticket.php` clears the children explicitly). MySQL refuses to add a FK while orphaned child rows exist (e.g. attachments left behind when the pre-fix delete removed an email but not its `email_attachments`); db_verify stays **non-destructive** — it never deletes data, so when orphans block a constraint it reports them as a `pending` item ("N orphaned row(s)… remove manually, then re-run") and moves on. This is what made the delete bug reproducible on fresh installs but invisible on older ones. |
| 538 | Tickets           | Fix         | **Deleting a ticket with an email attachment no longer fails with a foreign-key error.** `delete_ticket.php` deleted `emails` without first deleting the child `email_attachments` rows, so on installs where the `fk_email_attachments_email` constraint exists the delete failed with `1451 Cannot delete or update a parent row`. It also never cleared `ticket_audit` or `ticket_time_entries` (same no-cascade setup). Rewrote the delete to remove all children in FK-safe order inside a transaction (attachments → emails → notes → audit → time entries → ticket), roll back on error, and best-effort delete the now-orphaned attachment files from disk. |

| 535 | Tickets           | Fix         | **Tickets → Settings: header no longer gets pushed off-screen, and the waffle menu still works.** The page hard-coded `.container { height: calc(100vh - 48px) }` (assuming a one-line 48px header) on top of inbox.css's `body{overflow:hidden}`, so a taller/wrapping header plus a focus-triggered nudge-scroll — made worse by browser extensions (e.g. LastPass) injecting nodes around the focused field — could shove the top nav above the viewport with no way back. Fixed by wrapping the header + scrolling content in a plain flex wrapper (`.settings-shell`) so the header pins at the top and `.container` is the sole scroll region, with no fixed-height assumption. The header stays a normal *static* element (no `position`/flex on it or `<body>`), which avoids two traps: extension-injected `<body>` nodes can't become flex items, and the header doesn't become a stacking context that would hide the waffle menu panel behind its own close-overlay. |

| 508 | SSO               | Fix         | **OIDC sign-in no longer fails on providers that omit `email_verified` (e.g. Okta).** The callback gated login on `!empty($claims['email_verified'])`, which treats a *missing* claim the same as an explicit `false` &mdash; so every Okta sign-in was rejected with *"Your email is not verified with the identity provider"* even for a fully-verified account. Okta's org authorization server doesn't include `email_verified` in the ID token at all (Keycloak/Entra do). **Fix**: an explicit `email_verified: false` is still always rejected; a *missing* claim is now accepted by default, with a new per-provider **Require a verified-email claim** toggle (`auth_providers.require_verified_email`, default off) for admins running an IdP where users can self-register with unverified addresses. Surfaced while wiring up Okta as a second IdP alongside Keycloak. |

So on the landing page only, clicking Logout threw `Uncaught ReferenceError: showConfirm is not defined` and nothing happened (other module pages were fine because their header loads the waffle-menu JS). Fixed by loading `assets/js/toast.js` + `assets/js/confirm.js` directly on `index.php`; both self-guard against double-loading, so pages that already have them are unaffected. | 488 | CMDB              | Fix         | **Settings modal Cancel/Save buttons no longer sit hard against the edges.** Reported on Settings &rarr; Classes &rarr; Add. **Root cause**: the canonical settings-modal pattern has two distinct sticky-footer wrappers in `inbox.css`. `.modal-actions` is for **2-pane** modals (form fields directly inside `.modal-content`) &mdash; it only carries `padding-top: 12px` + sticky + a top border, relying on `.modal-content`'s own padding to provide horizontal space for the buttons. `.modal-footer` is for **3-pane** modals (form fields wrapped in `.modal-body`) &mdash; in the 3-pane case the `:has(> .modal-body)` rule zeroes `.modal-content`'s padding, so the footer brings its own `padding: 16px 24px`. CMDB settings has 3-pane modals (every Add/Edit form is wrapped in `.modal-body`) but used `.modal-actions`, so the buttons inherited sticky + top-border but **no horizontal padding** &mdash; they jammed against the modal edges. The recent #487 button-size cleanup made the buttons larger which made the squashed look obvious; the structural mismatch was actually older. **Fix**: swapped `.modal-actions` &rarr; `.modal-footer` on all five CMDB settings modals (class, properties manager, property, relationship type, AI suggest). The AI suggest modal's `id="aiSuggestActions"` (referenced by `settings.js`) is preserved &mdash; only the class changed. No JS references the class. The same bug exists on `cmdb/index.php` (New Object modal) and `cmdb/object.php` (Add Relationship + Set Parent modals) but is out of scope for this fix &mdash; flagged for a follow-up sweep along with the matching local `.btn` / `.btn-secondary` cleanup. |
| 482 | Tasks             | Fix         | **Timeline: dragging the right edge of a deadline-only task now extends the range, instead of moving the task.** Follow-up to #481. The `resize-r` mouseup handler only sent `due_date` in the save payload, so for a task that originally had no `start_date` (just a due-date) the start stayed NULL after the save &mdash; meaning the next render (`s = start_date || due_date; e = due_date || start_date`) showed the task as a single-day bar at the new due-date position rather than a multi-day range from the original due-date to the new one. **Fix**: also send `start_date = ds.origStart` in the `resize-r` payload. For a deadline-only task, `origStart === origEnd === old due_date`, so this pins the old due-date as the new start-date and the bar spans the dragged range exactly as the user expected. For a task that already has a start-date, `origStart` is the real start-date so the addition is a no-op. Resize-left and move paths already behaved correctly (left already pins `due_date` via the unchanged value, and move shifts both dates by the same delta). JS cache-buster bumped to `?v=8`. |
| 480 | Tasks             | Fix         | **Timeline: long date ranges now scroll horizontally instead of being squashed.** Follow-up to #479. The auto-fit calc was `dayW = max(8, available / rangeDays)` which kept stretching the grid edge-to-edge no matter how dense the range &mdash; for a 200-day range each day collapsed to ~8&ndash;10px and the day numbers disappeared, even though there was no horizontal scroll. **Flipped the rule** to `dayW = max(COMFORT_DAY_W, available / rangeDays)` with `COMFORT_DAY_W = 28`: ranges short enough that 28px per day fits the viewport still stretch to fill (the original "full width" goal), but as soon as the range gets long enough that days would shrink below 28px, we hold the floor and the timeline scrolls horizontally instead. Day numbers are always visible now since the floor guarantees a readable cell, so the `SHOW_NUM_W` branch + `showDayNum` flag are gone. JS cache-buster bumped to `?v=6`. |
| 477 | Tasks             | Fix         | **Tasks &rarr; Settings lookup modal (Add / Edit status, priority, tag): browser autocomplete disabled on the Name field.** Browser was offering past-typed values as a dropdown over the *Name* input &mdash; annoying when adding a new status/priority/tag that hadn't existed before. Added `autocomplete="off"` to both the `#lookupForm` (form-level, covers any future fields added to this modal) and the `#lookupItemName` text input directly (belt-and-braces because Chrome ignores the form-level attribute in some cases). Same modal is shared by all three lookup kinds via the `LOOKUP_KINDS` config so one fix covers Status / Priority / Tag. |

| 471 | Workflow          | Fix         | **Help-page sidebar scroll-to + scroll-spy now match every other module's behaviour.** Right after shipping the guide panel in #470 I'd written the click handler using `target.offsetTop - 16` and the scroll-spy threshold as `scrollTop + 80`. Cross-checked against the canonical pattern used by every other help page (tickets, asset-management, process-mapper, morning-checks, change-management, watchtower, software, calendar, tasks, knowledge): **(1)** clicks use `helpMain.getBoundingClientRect()` + `el.getBoundingClientRect()` to compute the actual distance from the scroll container's top edge, then `helpMain.scrollTo({ top: helpMain.scrollTop + (elTop - containerTop) - 20 })`. This is robust to any wrapper having positioning &mdash; whereas `offsetTop` measures from the nearest positioned ancestor, which is brittle. **(2)** scroll-spy threshold is `s.el.offsetTop - 200 <= scrollTop`, which fires the highlight earlier as the next heading approaches (smoother feel) rather than once it's already at the top of the viewport. Replaced both code paths to match the canonical idiom verbatim. |
| 469 | Workflow          | Fix         | **The *New* button is no longer underlined.** The Workflows list page's *New* button uses `<a class="add-btn" href="editor.php">` (an anchor that navigates to the editor page, rather than a `<button>` that opens a modal). The `.add-btn` rule in `inbox.css` didn't set `text-decoration: none`, so the browser's default anchor underline was bleeding through on every workflow page load. **Fix in `inbox.css`** (one-file fix at the source so it works for any future module that uses `.add-btn` on an `<a>`): added `text-decoration: none` and `display: inline-block` to `.add-btn`. Same pattern as the `.btn` rule which already has this for anchor-as-button cases (line 1482's existing comment was the prior art). |

| 467 | Morning Checks    | Fix         | **Modal buttons (Cancel / Save / Add / Create ticket / Map / Map all) now match every other module.** Inbox.css defines `.btn-primary` and `.btn-secondary` as *colour-only* (background + text colour) on top of a base `.btn` rule that provides the padding, border-radius, font-size, font-weight and transition. Every other module's modals use `class="btn btn-primary"` / `class="btn btn-secondary"`. | 447 | Docker            | Fix         | **Docker install was rendering a blank home page &mdash; `BASE_URL` was undefined in the container config.** Reported by a GitHub user who installed via `docker compose up`: home page showed nothing except the blue header bar and the avatar; console error *"Uncaught ReferenceError: toggleUserMenu is not defined"* on every avatar click. **Root cause**: `docker/config.php` (which is COPYd over the top of the local `config.php` at image-build time per the Dockerfile) defined the DB credentials but was missing the `BASE_URL` auto-detect block that the local config.php gained when `BASE_URL` was introduced. PHP 8.4 in the base image (`php:8.4-apache`) treats an undefined constant as a fatal `Error`, so the first `<?php echo BASE_URL; ?>` inside `renderHeaderRight()` (the *Preferences* link in the avatar menu) crashed the request mid-render. Apache had already flushed the avatar markup, so the browser saw header + avatar + abrupt EOF &mdash; no modules grid, no `<script>` block defining `toggleUserMenu`, no `</body>`. `display_errors = 0` in the Docker config meant the user got a silent blank page instead of a PHP error message. Now affects every Docker install because `BASE_URL` is used in 133 places across 26 files. **Fix**: ported the `BASE_URL` auto-detect block (the same one from `config.php:38-49`) into `docker/config.php`. Inside the standard image the app and doc root both live at `/var/www/html`, so it resolves to `/`, which matches users hitting `http://localhost:8080/`. |

| 418 | Morning checks    | Fix         | **Chart height preference fetched server-side so the first paint is already at the user's chosen size &mdash; no more snap on load.** Previously the page rendered at the CSS default `height: 280px` from `style.css`, then once the JS `loadChartHeightPref()` AJAX call completed (~100ms later) the height jumped to the saved percentage. **Now**: a PHP block at the top of the page reads `user_preferences` directly (key `mc_chart_height_pct`, clamped 12&ndash;80) and emits the value into an inline `style="height: calc((100vh - 60px) * <fraction>)"` on `.chart-container-inner`. The 60px is the global header's approximate height &mdash; the calc gets us very close on first paint; JS reconciles to the exact pixel value on `DOMContentLoaded` via `lockChartHeightFromInitial()` so any sub-pixel mismatch is invisible. The dedicated JS `loadChartHeightPref()` is now redundant (the value also gets emitted as a `const INITIAL_CHART_PCT` so the JS module starts with the correct base), so it's been replaced with the lock-from-initial call &mdash; saves one AJAX round-trip too. |

| 391 | Knowledge         | Fix         | **Articles authored by since-deleted analysts no longer disappear from the list.** Follow-up to #390 &mdash; #390 closed the *unpublished drafts* gap between the tag count and the filtered list, but the user still saw e.g. *"Email (3)"* show only one article on click. **Root cause**: `knowledge_articles.php`, `knowledge_article.php` and `knowledge_archive.php` all used `INNER JOIN analysts an ON an.id = a.author_id` so any article whose author was later deleted from the analysts table silently dropped out of every list, while the tag-count subquery still counted them. **Fix**: switched all three queries to `LEFT JOIN analysts` and wrapped `an.full_name` in `COALESCE(..., '(deleted analyst)')` so orphaned articles still show up with a sensible fallback in the byline. | 388 | Assets            | Fix         | **Assets settings page hard-refresh time dropped from ~4.5s to ~0.75s.** Classic PHP session-locking foot-gun: the page fires *six* AJAX requests on load (asset types, asset statuses, system settings for vCenter + InTune, last InTune sync, recent app-sync jobs, inventory freshness chart) and every endpoint called the default `session_start()` &mdash; which acquires an exclusive `flock` on the session file for the duration of the request. With one session per analyst, all six requests serialised behind that lock at roughly 750ms each = ~4.5s wall-clock. **Fix**: changed `session_start()` &rarr; `session_start(['read_and_close' => true])` on the six endpoints involved, which opens the session, populates `$_SESSION` for the auth check, and immediately releases the lock so the requests run in actual parallel. Same six-fold speedup. **Note**: a grep showed *no* endpoint in `api/` currently uses `session_write_close` / `read_and_close`, so the same slowdown almost certainly affects every other page that fires multiple AJAX calls on load (dashboards, settings pages in other modules, the asset table view's preferences load + assets list, etc.). Offered a follow-up sweep. |

| 372 | System            | Fix         | **Sticky navbar restored across ~40 module pages that were overriding `body { overflow: hidden; height: 100vh }`.** Follow-up to #371 &mdash; the navbar-consistency pass uncovered a much wider issue: every settings page, the workflow / rfp-builder / system admin pages, and the dashboard / library / intune pages were all carrying a `body { overflow: auto; height: auto; }` block inside their inline `<style>` that overrode the `inbox.css` rule meant to pin the navbar at the top. When the page scrolled, the body scrolled with it and the navbar disappeared. **Fix**: removed those body overrides and moved the scrolling onto each page's own outer wrapper instead (`.container` / `.settings-container` / `.branding-container` / `.prefs-container` / `.debug-container` / `.demo-container` / `.security-container` / `.colours-container` / `.db-verify-container` / `.csat-page` / `.obj-page` / `.status-layout` / `.page-wrap` / `.rfp-view-wrap` &mdash; whichever that page actually used), each given `height: calc(100vh - 48px); overflow-y: auto` so the navbar stays fixed and the wrapper scrolls independently. Dashboard / library / intune pages had no single outer wrapper (toolbar + grid were sibling top-level children), so they got a new `.dashboard-page` wrapping div with the same scroll rules. ~40 files touched: tickets / workflow / process-mapper / tasks / cmdb / service-status / change-management / forms / contracts / asset-management / knowledge / software / morning-checks / calendar settings pages; tickets/csat + cmdb/object + service-status + rfp-builder/* + system/* admin pages; tickets/dashboard/(index+library), asset-management/dashboard/(index+library), software/dashboard/(index+library), reporting/intune. Self-service portal pages and the root landing page are deliberately excluded (they use a different layout model). |
| 367 | Tickets           | Fix         | **CSAT survey templates now save without an *"Invalid trigger"* error.** Follow-up to #365: the new `csat_request` event was added to the template editor's dropdown but `api/tickets/save_email_template.php` had a hardcoded `$validEvents` whitelist that didn't know about it, so trying to save would fail at the server-side check. Added `csat_request` to the whitelist. |
| 366 | Tickets           | Fix         | **CSAT *Request feedback* now fails loudly when no template / mailbox exists, instead of falsely reporting success.** First real test of #365 surfaced the trap: clicking the button created a `ticket_csat_responses` row with a token but `sendTemplateEmail()` silently no-op'd because there was no active `csat_request` template configured yet &mdash; the analyst saw *"Survey email sent"*, no email arrived, and the orphan token sat in the database forever. `sendCsatSurvey()` now does pre-flight checks (active template exists, ticket has a sendable mailbox) BEFORE creating the row, and returns a structured `{result, response_id}` so callers can give honest UI messages. `api/tickets/request_csat.php` switches on the result code to surface a specific error per failure mode &mdash; e.g. *"No active CSAT survey template found. Add one under Tickets &rarr; Settings &rarr; Email templates with event 'CSAT survey' (and remember to include the [csat_link] placeholder in the body)."* Auto-trigger path in `assign_ticket.php` is unchanged behaviourally (still fire-and-forget; failures log to error_log) but no longer leaves orphan rows on a missed template. Cleared 2 orphan rows from the first test session so the analytics page's response-rate denominator starts clean. |
| 364 | System            | Fix         | **Landing page (`index.php`) now shows all 20 modules &mdash; Workflows and CMDB were missing.** The post-login module-selection grid only showed 18 cards (Watchtower, Tickets, Assets, Knowledge, Changes, Calendar, Morning Checks, Reporting, Software, Forms, Contracts, Service Status, Wiki, LMS, Process Mapper, Tasks, Network Mapper, System) &mdash; both CMDB (#290+ vintage) and Workflows (#340 vintage) had been added to the in-app waffle menu, the colour map (`includes/module-colors.php`), the i18n catalogue (`lang/en/common.php`), and the per-analyst module-access settings, but the landing page itself was never updated to include them. Ordering matches the waffle: CMDB sits between Tasks and Network Mapper, Workflows between Network Mapper and System. The `allowed_modules` check uses the canonical `'cmdb'` / `'workflow'` keys so per-analyst module access controls work without further changes. Grid is now 20 cards in a 7-column layout = 2 full rows of 7 plus a final row of 6, more visually balanced than the previous 18 = 2 rows of 7 + row of 4. |
| 363 | Self-Service      | Fix         | **Submitting a ticket with an un-attached recording now blocks instead of silently dropping it.** First real test of #362 surfaced an easy-to-miss UX trap &mdash; after clicking Stop the user sees a preview with *Use this* / *Discard* buttons, but if they ignored those buttons and clicked Submit, the recording sat in JS memory as `recordedBlob` and was silently lost (the ticket posted with an empty `recording_ids` array). The recording was never uploaded, never claimed, never visible to the analyst. **Fix**: `handleSubmit()` now checks `recordedBlob !== null` at the top and short-circuits if there's an unclaimed blob &mdash; expands the panel back open (in case it was collapsed), `scrollIntoView`s it, and replaces the status line with a red-text instruction: *"Click **Use this** to attach the recording, or **Discard** to drop it &mdash; then submit again."* No silent loss possible; the user gets an unambiguous next action. `discardRecording()` now also clears the inline red colour/weight so the status returns to its normal "Ready" look when the next recording starts. |
| 361 | Tickets           | Fix         | **Browser autofill disabled on the Add/Edit user modal.** Without `autocomplete` hints, browsers were happy to suggest the *analyst's own* email / password into a form whose entire purpose is creating an *end user* &mdash; a recipe for accidentally typing one's own credentials into someone else's record. Set `autocomplete="off"` on the form and on each text/email input, and `autocomplete="new-password"` on the password input (Chrome ignores `off` on password fields by design, but respects `new-password` as the signal that this is account creation, not a login). |
| 360 | Tickets           | Fix         | **Add/Edit user modal title no longer indented.** Follow-up to #359 &mdash; once `.modal-content` was given 30px padding, the modal-header's own default `padding: 20px 24px` from `inbox.css` stacked on top and the *Add user* title appeared indented from the left edge of the form fields below it. The settings page strips this for the same reason (`padding: 0; border-bottom: none; margin-bottom: 20px`); did the same here, scoped to `#userModal .modal-header`. |
| 359 | Tickets           | Fix         | **Add/Edit user modal now compact and padded like the analyst modal.** The new user CRUD modal from #358 was rendering at 900px wide with zero internal padding because `tickets/users.php` was inheriting the default `.modal-content` rule from `inbox.css` (designed for the wide content modals like the mailbox config dialog). The analyst modal in `tickets/settings/` looks right because that page ships a page-level `.modal-content { padding: 30px; max-width: 500px; }` override. Added the same override here, but scoped to `#userModal .modal-content` so it only applies to this modal and can't accidentally restyle anything else added later on the same page. |
| 355 | Workflows         | Fix         | **Ticket dispatches now carry the full current ticket state, and *Test fire* builds a synthetic payload from the workflow's own conditions.** Two bugs in #354 surfaced the moment a real workflow ran: **(1)** the `ticket.assigned` dispatch payload was `{ticket: {id}, analyst_id, team_id}` &mdash; only the ticket's id, not its other fields &mdash; so a perfectly reasonable condition like *priority is Critical* read `null` from `ticket.priority_id` and the engine correctly marked the run *skipped*. Same shape problem affected `ticket.status_changed` / `ticket.priority_changed` &mdash; each only carried a couple of sibling fields beyond the changed one. **Fix:** `api/tickets/assign_ticket.php` now reads back the FULL post-update ticket row once (id, subject, priority_id, status_id, department_id, type_id, assigned_analyst_id, owner_id, origin_id, created_by, plus requester_email joined from `users`) and includes that canonical `ticket` payload in every dispatch &mdash; so any condition on any ticket field works regardless of which trigger fired. Engine `availableFields()` widened to match: every `ticket.*` trigger's field hints now lists the full ticket field set plus the event-specific extras (old_/new_ ids, analyst_id, team_id), reused from a single `$fullTicket` array so they can't drift apart. **(2)** *Test fire* in the editor sent `payload: {}` (empty), which meant any workflow with any condition would always report *skipped* &mdash; the button was misleading users into thinking their workflow was broken when actually the test harness was broken. **Fix:** new `buildTestFirePayload()` in `workflow-editor.js` synthesises a payload from the workflow's own conditions: equality ops get `payload[field] = value` (first item if it's a list), inequality ops get a sentinel that won't match, contains gets the value embedded in a longer string, gt/lt get value&plusmn;1, is_empty/is_not_empty get `""`/`"x"`. Result: Test fire now means *"do my actions run when conditions pass"* &mdash; the workflow's conditions all trivially pass against the synthetic payload, so the action path actually executes and the user sees a real success/failed status. `workflow-editor.js` &rarr; `?v=7`. |
| 350 | Tickets           | Fix         | **You can now assign / change a ticket's priority from the open-ticket toolbar.** Priority could only be set at creation time (from the new-ticket modal), with no UI for changing it on an existing ticket &mdash; the detail-panel toolbar had Department, Type, Status, Origin, First Time Fix, IT Training, Owner, but no Priority dropdown. Added a Priority `<select>` to the toolbar between Status and Origin, sourced from the `ticket_priorities` lookup (active-only, ordered by display_order). Blank option lets you clear the priority (it's nullable). `assignPriority()` posts to `assign_ticket.php` and logs the change to the audit trail; the SLA engine is compute-on-read so it recomputes lazily on the next ticket fetch &mdash; no explicit recompute call needed. Backend changes: `api/tickets/assign_ticket.php` now accepts `priority_id` (null clears), `api/tickets/get_email_detail.php` returns `t.priority_id` alongside the existing `tp.name AS priority` so the dropdown can pre-select the current value. New `loadTicketPriorities()` runs at init, mirroring the existing `loadTicketStatuses` / `loadTicketTypes` pattern, with results filtered to `is_active`. `inbox.js` &rarr; `?v=24`. |
| 349 | System            | Fix         | **Waffle-menu fix: Workflows icon was missing its background colour; grid now four columns wide.** Two related tweaks to the waffle menu that drops down from the top-left of every module page. (1) The Workflows module was registered in the menu's `$modules` array (since #340) but never added to `includes/module-colors.php`'s `$defaultModuleColors` map, so the waffle's per-module gradient rule (`.waffle-module-icon.<key>`) had no entry for it &mdash; the icon rendered with no background and the SVG was an invisible white glyph on white. Added `'workflow' =&gt; ['#ea580c', '#c2410c']` (Tailwind orange-600 to orange-700) &mdash; distinct enough from contracts' amber to be tellable apart in the icon grid while staying in the same "automation" colour family. (2) `.waffle-modules` grid changed from `repeat(3, 1fr)` to `repeat(4, 1fr)` so the 20 modules render as a 4&times;5 grid instead of 3&times;7 &mdash; less scrolling, more glanceable. `.waffle-panel min-width` bumped from 360px to 460px so the 4-column grid has breathing room for the icon + label per cell. |
| 347 | Workflows         | Fix         | **Multi-select for lookup-field conditions is now the default, not hidden behind a deliberate operator switch.** Follow-up to #346 &mdash; the multi-select capability was there, but the user had to discover that flipping the operator dropdown from *equals* to *is one of* unlocked it, which is the kind of secret-handshake UX that absolutely nobody finds. The condition panel now always shows a checkbox list for lookup fields (priority / status / department / type / analyst / team / etc.) regardless of operator, and the operator dropdown for lookup fields is collapsed down to just **is**, **is not**, **is empty**, **is not empty** &mdash; mapping internally to `in` / `not_in` / `is_empty` / `is_not_empty`. Tick one box for an exact match (the engine treats `in` with a 1-item array identically to `equals`), tick several for OR semantics. Legacy `equals` / `not_equals` conditions on lookup fields get silently upgraded to `in` / `not_in` the first time the user opens them so the rebuilt UI stays consistent &mdash; behaviour preserved because the engine handles both. Free-text fields still get the full operator catalogue (contains, gt, lt, etc.). The op dropdown auto-rebuilds when the field changes, so flipping between a lookup and a free-text field instantly swaps the available operators. `workflow-editor.js` &rarr; `?v=5`. |
| 345 | Workflows         | Fix         | **Workflow editor lets you save in-progress drafts without at least one action.** The original Save flow blocked client-side AND server-side with *"At least one action is required"*, but that's actively unhelpful while building a workflow step-by-step (pick a trigger &rarr; add conditions &rarr; <em>and now you can't save your progress until you stub an action</em>). The engine itself tolerates zero actions &mdash; the action loop just doesn't run, and the execution row is logged as a normal success/skipped run with an empty step log &mdash; so the only thing the strict gate enforced was the friction. Removed the check in `assets/js/workflow-editor.js` `save()` and the mirror in `api/workflow/save.php`; on a successful save with zero actions the user gets a soft *info* toast (*"Saved — but this workflow has no actions yet, so it won't do anything until you add one"*) instead of being blocked. New i18n key `workflow.toast.saved_no_actions`. `workflow-editor.js` &rarr; `?v=3`. |
| 344 | Workflows         | Fix         | **AI Test button respects the global `SSL_VERIFY_PEER` kill switch from `config.php`.** Dev installs without a CA bundle wired into php.ini run with `SSL_VERIFY_PEER = false` so every outbound HTTPS skips peer verification &mdash; but the workflow AI Test / compose calls were ignoring it and only honouring the per-form Verify SSL toggle on the settings page. Testing an Anthropic / OpenAI key on a dev install therefore failed with `Failed: Network error: SSL certificate problem: unable to get local issuer certificate`. Added a tiny helper `workflowEffectiveSslVerify(bool $perCallVerify): bool` in `api/workflow/_ai_helpers.php` that ANDs the global constant with the per-form toggle, and routed all four curl call sites &mdash; `wfCallAnthropic` + `wfCallOpenAI` in `_ai_helpers.php` and `wfTestAnthropic` + `wfTestOpenAI` in `test_ai_key.php` &mdash; through it. The per-form toggle still works as before for production installs where the global is true (e.g. corporate inspecting proxy with a self-signed cert needs to opt out of verification for one integration without disabling globally). The same fix in the RFP module's curl drivers is a separate pre-existing bug not in scope here. |
| 339 | Process Mapper    | Fix         | **Collapsed left panel was leaking the left edges of its contents through the 16px hot-zone.** The "Show on hover" sidebar mode (#338) clips the sidebar to a 16px strip via `overflow: hidden`, but the children (the "+ New" button, the search box, the process list) were still rendered &mdash; you could see a thin slice of each control peeking out of the strip, which looked unfinished. Added a `.pm-layout.sidebar-hover .pm-sidebar > *` rule that sets `opacity: 0; pointer-events: none` on the direct children of the collapsed sidebar; on `:hover` they fade back in (`opacity: 1`) with an `0.08s` transition delay so they don't appear over a half-expanded strip mid-slide. The vertical strip indicator (`::before` pseudo-element) is unaffected by the `>` selector, so the hoverability hint stays visible. `process-mapper.css` &rarr; `?v=10`. |
| 337 | Process Mapper    | Fix         | **URL badge was invisible on diamond / hexagon / trapezoid / cloud steps and hung in empty space outside circle / pill steps.** The badge was positioned at `top: 4px; right: 4px;` (bbox top-right corner) which works for rectangular shapes, but the bounding-box top-right falls outside the visible region for several others. For clip-path shapes (diamond, hexagon, trapezoid, cloud) `clip-path` clips descendants too &mdash; the badge was being clipped away entirely. For border-radius shapes (circle, pill) the badge wasn't clipped, but it floated in transparent space outside the coloured fill, looking detached from the step. Added per-shape `[data-shape="..."] .pm-step-url-badge` positioning rules that pull the badge inward into a spot that's reliably inside the visible region across the default size range &mdash; diamond at `top: 26%; right: 30%;` (inside the polygon's top-right slope), hexagon / trapezoid at `top: 6px; right: 28%;` (inside the flat top edge), cloud at `top: 18%; right: 22%;` (inside the middle ellipse), circle at `top: 14%; right: 18%;` (inside the top-right arc), pill at `top: 6px; right: 32px;` (past the right rounded end-cap). `process-mapper.css` &rarr; `?v=8`. |
| 332 | Process Mapper    | Fix         | **PNG / PDF export was clipping content reachable only by scrolling sideways.** `.pm-canvas` is a scroll container (`overflow: auto`), and `html2canvas` uses the element's CSS box as its rendering bounds &mdash; so any step sitting beyond the visible viewport was being chopped off the export even though the bounding-box rect we passed in clearly extended past it. Fixed by temporarily expanding the canvas during capture: in `captureCanvas()`, before calling `html2canvas`, the canvas is given an explicit `width`/`height` equal to `max(scrollWidth, rect.x + rect.width)` × `max(scrollHeight, rect.y + rect.height)`, switched to `overflow: visible`, and pulled out of its parent's flex layout with `flex: 0 0 auto`. The connector SVG layer is pinned to the same expanded dimensions because some browsers compute its `width: 100%` from the scroll viewport rather than the new box. All four properties (plus the SVG attrs and the scroll position) are stashed before mutation and restored in the `finally` block so a thrown exception can't leave the canvas mis-sized. `.pm-canvas-wrap` already has `overflow: hidden` so the user doesn't see the canvas balloon during the ~half-second capture. `process-mapper.js` &rarr; `?v=7`. |
| 313 | Tasks             | Fix         | **Tasks module pages now cache-bust their CSS/JS** with `?v=` query strings on `tasks.css`, `tasks.js`, `tasks-calendar.js` and `tasks-timeline.js` (board, calendar, timeline and settings pages). The tasks module was the only one without cache-busting, so JS/CSS changes &mdash; such as the new Start Date field in the detail panel &mdash; would not appear until users manually hard-refreshed. |
| 315 | Tasks             | Fix         | **Stray main-window scrollbar on the Tasks board, calendar and timeline.** `tasks.css` set the `body` to `overflow:auto` and `.tasks-container` to `height:calc(100vh - 50px)`, which assumed a 50px-tall header &mdash; but the real header has no fixed height and renders ~56px (`padding:12px 20px`), so header + container overflowed the viewport by a few pixels and the browser added a vertical scrollbar. Replaced the hardcoded maths with a proper flex layout: `body` is `height:100vh; overflow:hidden; display:flex; flex-direction:column`, the header is `flex-shrink:0`, and `.tasks-container` is `flex:1; min-height:0` &mdash; so the content fills the viewport exactly regardless of header height, with no clipping and no stray scrollbar. The settings page (which legitimately scrolls) re-asserts `display:block` in its own stylesheet. `tasks.css` bumped to `?v=4`. |
| 317 | Tasks             | Fix         | **Drag-reorder drop indicator invisible in scrolling board columns.** The purple line that shows where a dragged card will land vanished whenever its column had enough cards to scroll. Cause: `.board-cards` is a `flex-direction:column` container and the `.drop-indicator` is an empty `<div>` &mdash; so its min-content height is 0, and when the column overflowed, flexbox's `flex-shrink` compressed the indicator to 0px (the cards resist because their text gives them a min-content height; the empty indicator does not). Fixed by adding `flex-shrink:0` to `.drop-indicator` (and to `.task-card` for good measure, so cards can never be squished either). `tasks.css` bumped to `?v=6`. |

### 30 May 2026

| ID  | Module            | Type        | Description |

| 506 | Authentication    | Feature     | **SSO Stage D — migration tooling, email-first login, SSO-only enforcement, single logout, JIT access control.** Four pieces completing the SSO build. **(1) Assign existing analyst → provider**: the analyst editor (Tickets → Settings → Analysts) gains a *Sign-in method* dropdown (Local, or any configured provider); `save_analyst.php`/`get_analysts.php` carry `auth_provider_id`. This is how pre-existing users are migrated to SSO (only JIT set the assignment before) — on their next SSO sign-in their identity links automatically by email. **(2) Email-first login router**: the login page now leads with an email box → new `api/auth/resolve_login.php` looks up the email and, if it belongs to an active analyst assigned to an enabled provider, redirects straight to that provider; otherwise it falls back to the local form (returns `local` for unknown emails too, so it never reveals whether an account exists). Provider buttons remain as a shortcut (the "both" UX). **(3) Login layout + SSO-only + break-glass**: whenever SSO is active the local username/password form is tucked behind a "Sign in with a local account" link by default (the page leads with the email-first router + provider buttons); the email-first fallback or the link reveals it. Turning *Allow local login* off also hides that link (true SSO-only look), while `?local=1` and the master SSO kill switch keep break-glass open — local auth is never hard-blocked, by design, so no one can be locked out. **(4) Single logout**: `analyst_logout.php` now, for SSO sessions, redirects to the provider's `end_session_endpoint` (with `id_token_hint` + `post_logout_redirect_uri`) so signing out of FreeITSM also ends the IdP session; the callback stashes `sso_provider_id` + `sso_id_token` for this. **(5) JIT access control**: the provider config modal exposes the `default_modules` field (comma-separated module keys granted to auto-created users) with an explicit warning that leaving it blank grants full access — so JIT pilots don't silently create admins. Verified: email resolver routes the assigned test user to SSO and unknown emails to local; login page renders email-first + buttons. |
| 505 | Authentication    | Feature     | **SSO login goes live — sign in via OpenID Connect (Stage C of the SSO build).** Users can now actually log in through a configured provider (Keycloak/Entra/Okta/Google/etc.) from the login page. **Flow**: a "Sign in with <provider>" button on `login.php` (rendered per enabled provider, only when `sso_enabled`) → `api/auth/oidc_login.php` (Authorization Code + **PKCE S256**, generates `state`/`nonce`/verifier into the session, redirects to the IdP) → IdP authenticates → `api/auth/oidc_callback.php` validates `state`, exchanges the code at the token endpoint (back-channel, client secret), and **validates the ID token's signature against the provider's JWKS** plus issuer/audience/nonce/expiry. **JWT validation uses the vendored `firebase/php-jwt` v6.11.0** (`includes/vendor/firebase-jwt/`, committed — no Composer in this project) — never hand-rolled. **Account resolution**: existing identity link (`provider_id`+`sub`) → email match (requires `email_verified`) → just-in-time create (only if the provider's `auto_create_users` is on). **Strict pilot isolation**: an analyst may only sign in via the provider their `auth_provider_id` is set to; a mismatch is rejected, so an SSO login can't silently take over a local or other-provider account. JIT-created analysts are stamped with `auth_provider_id` + linked, given an unusable random local password, and granted the provider's `default_modules` (empty = full access). **SSO logins set the session directly and skip the local TOTP/MFA step** (the IdP owns MFA). New shared helper `includes/oidc.php` (discovery + per-request cache, authorize-URL builder, code exchange, ID-token validation, curl wrappers respecting `SSL_VERIFY_PEER`). All errors bounce back to `login.php` with a readable message via a session flash. Verified end-to-end against a local Keycloak (realm `freeitsm`, JIT auto-created the test user and logged them straight in). **Known gap (next)**: no UI yet to assign an *existing* analyst to a provider — only JIT sets the assignment automatically; needed for migrating pre-existing users to SSO. |
| 504 | Authentication    | Feature     | **SSO admin config page — add/manage OIDC identity providers (Stage B of the SSO build).** New **System → Single Sign-On** page (`system/sso/index.php`, card added to the system landing grid) to configure providers before any login wiring. **Global settings card**: two break-glass toggles — *Enable single sign-on* (master switch, shows provider buttons; off = instant fallback to local) and *Allow local login* (keep the username/password form so a down IdP can't lock everyone out) — stored in `system_settings` (`sso_enabled` / `local_login_enabled`) via the existing generic `api/settings/get_system_settings.php` + `save_system_settings.php`. **Redirect URI card**: shows the exact callback URL (built from `BASE_URL` → `<scheme>://<host>/freeitsm-app/api/auth/oidc_callback.php`) with a copy button, to paste into each IdP. **Identity providers card**: a table of configured providers (name, issuer, enabled badge, JIT badge) with an add/edit modal — fields are display name (login button label), issuer URL, client ID, client secret, scopes (default `openid email profile`), *Enabled* and *Auto-create users (JIT)* toggles. | 503 | Authentication    | Feature     | **SSO foundation — database schema for multi-provider OIDC login (Stage A of the SSO build).** Lays the groundwork for "Sign in with Keycloak/Entra/Okta" alongside the existing username+password+TOTP login.
