| 502 | Assets            | Feature     | **Warranty-expiry alerts — surfaced on the Watchtower dashboard and/or the Calendar, configurable in settings.** Closes the "surface warranty expiries" half of the procurement work (the fields shipped in #498). New **Asset Settings → Warranty alerts** tab lets you choose where expiries show up — *Off / Watchtower dashboard / Calendar / Both* — plus a "warn N days before expiry" threshold (default 30; already-expired assets always count). Stored in `system_settings` (`asset_warranty_surface`, `asset_warranty_days`). **Watchtower**: the Assets card gains a red "Warranty" metric + attention line ("N asset(s) with warranty expired or expiring within X days") when the dashboard surface is enabled (count computed in `includes/watchtower_queries.php`, gated + defensive against the column not existing yet; card render in `watchtower/index.php` turns the status dot red). **Calendar**: assets with a warranty date get an all-day event in an auto-created "Warranty" category. Rather than a cron, a shared helper `includes/asset_warranty_calendar.php` (`syncAssetWarrantyCalendar`) does a full resync — it's called whenever an asset's warranty date changes (`update_asset_field.php`) and when the setting is saved (new `api/assets/sync_warranty_calendar.php`), deleting + reinserting only its own `source='asset_warranty'` events so manual events are untouched. | 497 | Assets            | Feature     | **Asset Settings → new *Locations* tab: build an arbitrary-depth location hierarchy.** First piece of the Snipe-IT-style lifecycle layer. New `asset_locations` table is an **adjacency list** (`id`, `name`, `parent_id` self-referencing FK, `display_order`) so locations nest as deep or shallow as wanted and every branch is independent — e.g. `UK › London › Office 1` next to a flat `Datacentre`, and you can add a third level to one branch without touching another. New endpoints `api/assets/get_asset_locations.php` (flat list, client builds the tree), `save_asset_location.php` (create/update name + parent; **re-parenting with cycle protection** — a node can't be moved under itself or a descendant, validated by walking up the ancestor chain server-side), and `delete_asset_location.php` (**refuses to delete a node that still has children** so a branch can't be wiped by accident; the DB self-ref FK is RESTRICT as a backstop). The Locations tab renders a collapsible indented tree: each node has a caret (collapse/expand), a child count, and hover actions — **+** (add sub-location, pre-fills the parent), edit (rename / re-parent via a parent dropdown that shows the hierarchy indented and excludes the node's own subtree), and delete. | 493 | Workflow          | Improvement | **Infinite-loop protection in the engine &mdash; a workflow can no longer trigger itself into a runaway chain.** With all seven triggers now firing (#492), a workflow whose action mutates host data that re-dispatches an event could in principle loop: directly (A fires an event that re-runs A) or via a cycle (A &rarr; B &rarr; A), or blow up via fan-out (one event spawning an ever-growing set of runs). Execution is synchronous within a single PHP request, so `WorkflowEngine::run()` is now a thin guard wrapper around the real body (renamed `runInner()`) backed by three request-scoped counters: **(1) an active-workflow stack** &mdash; a workflow already executing in the current chain is refused re-entry, which catches *every* cycle since a cycle must revisit a workflow still on the stack; **(2) `MAX_CHAIN_DEPTH` (10)** &mdash; a hard nesting-depth ceiling as a backstop for an absurdly deep but acyclic cascade; **(3) `MAX_RUNS_PER_REQUEST` (100)** &mdash; a per-request total-run ceiling as a backstop for fan-out blow-ups where each run spawns new, distinct workflows. The stack-pop and depth-decrement run in a `finally` so one throwing run can't wedge the counters for the rest of the request. A blocked run is **still recorded** &mdash; new `recordAbortedRun()` writes a `workflow_executions` row with a new **`aborted`** status, a `loop_protection` step-log entry, and a human-readable reason, and stamps the parent workflow's `last_run_status = 'aborted'` (without bumping `run_count`, since nothing actually executed) so the block is visible in the audit. The editor's recent-executions panel renders `aborted` as a distinct red pill (new `workflow.status.aborted` i18n string); `freeitsm.sql` status-column comments updated to list `aborted` (no schema change &mdash; the column is already `VARCHAR(20)`). Editor JS cache-buster `?v=8` &rarr; `?v=9`. |
| 492 | Workflow          | Feature     | **Forms, Tasks and Change Management now fire real workflow triggers &mdash; the last three catalogued events go live (Stage 5 complete).** Until now only the four `ticket.*` events were wired from a host module; `form.submitted`, `task.completed` and `change.approved` existed in `WorkflowEngine::availableTriggers()` (so the editor offered them) but no module actually dispatched them. Each host save flow now `require_once`s `workflow/includes/engine.php` and calls `WorkflowEngine::dispatch()` after its successful write, wrapped in a defensive try/catch (the engine already swallows internally &mdash; belt+braces so an engine outage can't break the host request). **(1) `form.submitted`** &mdash; `api/forms/submit_form.php` dispatches after the submission commits. Payload carries `form.id` / `form.name` / `submission.id` plus `submission.email` (the first email-type answer, surfaced because new-starter-style forms key off it) and a bonus `submission.fields` map of every answer keyed by its field label &mdash; so an action template can reference `{{submission.fields.Department}}` etc., powering the marquee "new starter form &rarr; tickets in IT / HR / Facilities" fan-out. **(2) `task.completed`** &mdash; `api/tasks/save.php` dispatches from the update path, but **only on the transition into a closed status**: it reads the task's current `task_statuses.is_closed` *before* the UPDATE and fires only when the task moved from an open status into a closed one (re-saving an already-done task does nothing). | 479 | Tasks             | Improvement | **Timeline view now auto-fits the available width &mdash; zoom controls removed.** Previously the timeline used four discrete zoom levels (`DAY_WIDTHS = [14, 22, 34, 52]`) with `+` / `&minus;` buttons on the right of the toolbar. The default mid-zoom worked OK for ranges of a few weeks but typical task sets either left half the timeline empty (sparse range) or overflowed off-screen (dense range), and the user had to manually find the right zoom each time. **Replaced** with a single auto-computed `dayW = (host.clientWidth - LABEL_W - SCROLLBAR_PAD) / rangeDays`, clamped to a minimum of 8px so very long ranges still render (and scroll horizontally if needed). For typical ranges (sub-year), the grid now spans edge-to-edge with no horizontal scroll. **Day-number labels hidden** when `dayW < 12` (would be illegible) &mdash; the month band stays so the date context is still visible. **Window resize triggers a debounced re-render** (150ms) so the grid re-fits when the user resizes the browser or expands/collapses the sidebar. **Removed**: `DAY_WIDTHS`, `zoomIndex`, the `zoom(dir)` function, the `.tl-zoom` markup + CSS rule, the toolbar's right-side zoom cluster (the toolbar now just shows *Today* + the date range on the left). | 451 | System            | Improvement | **App-wide standardisation of toast notifications + confirmation dialogs.** One shared `showToast(message, type)` and one shared `showConfirm({...})` now drive every notification and OK/Cancel dialog across FreeITSM, so the look and feel is tweakable in exactly one place. **What was there before**: a working global `assets/js/toast.js` (#432, with the per-analyst position / animation preferences from System &rarr; Preferences) but only ~6 of 14 settings pages actually imported it; the rest defined their own local `showToast(message, isError)` helpers with subtly different signatures + styling. Confirms were a mix of native `confirm()` (~70 calls), a one-off `customAlert` library used only by Knowledge, and a hand-rolled `<div id="confirmModal">` markup duplicated into the Calendar settings page. Native `alert()` was scattered across ~50 files (~135 calls), often passing a single string with no clue about success vs error context. **What changed**: **(1) New `assets/js/confirm.js`** &mdash; a Promise-based shared OK/Cancel dialog modelled visually on the Calendar settings delete-category modal the user called out as the canonical look (header / message body / footer with Cancel + Delete buttons, ESC to dismiss, click-backdrop to dismiss, Enter to confirm, autofocus on OK). API: `showConfirm({title, message, okLabel, okClass: 'primary'|'danger', onConfirm, onCancel})` returns a Promise<boolean> so callers can either `await` it or pass an `onConfirm` callback. Auto-injects its own markup + CSS on first call so no page needs scaffolding. **(2) Global loading** &mdash; both `toast.js` and `confirm.js` now load from `waffle-menu.php`'s `renderWaffleMenuJS()` block, which is included on every analyst-facing page. Individual `<script src=...toast.js>` tags removed from 19+ pages. **(3) Settings pages** (14 files) &mdash; every local `showToast(msg, isError)` / `showConfirm(title, msg, cb, ...)` definition deleted; every native `alert()` swapped to `showToast(msg, 'error'|'success')` using a heuristic that detects success contexts via the literal word "successfully" in the message; every native `confirm()` swapped to `showConfirm({...})` with `'danger'` styling for delete / remove / "cannot be undone" wording and `'primary'` otherwise. Inline `<span class="save-message">Saved!</span>` patterns in Knowledge / Contracts settings replaced with toast calls. Inline `<div class="toast">` markup removed everywhere it was duplicated. **(4) Module pages** &mdash; same sweep across ~35 more files: asset-management, calendar, change-management, cmdb (browse / object / settings JS files), contracts (contacts, suppliers, supplier view, rfp-builder consolidate/document/documents/extracted/index/suppliers/view), forms (edit + dashboard), network-mapper, service-status, software (dashboard library + licences), system (demo-data + encryption + modules), tickets (dashboard library + users), workflow. Plus the heavy-lifters in `assets/js/`: inbox.js, knowledge.js, lms.js, process-mapper.js, tasks.js, change-management.js, itsm_calendar.js, rota.js. Functions that previously contained native `confirm()` were marked `async` where they weren't already, so the `await showConfirm(...)` pattern works end-to-end. **(5) Customised cases handled manually**: the legacy `customAlert` library (used only by Knowledge) was migrated to `showConfirm` / `showToast` and the file deleted; the legacy `includes/header.php` logout and the waffle-menu logout button both converted to `showConfirm({onConfirm: () => navigate})` callback style since they're inline HTML attribute handlers; the Forms dashboard's custom `<div id="confirmOverlay">` delete confirmation replaced with `showConfirm`. **Validation**: final sweep confirms zero `alert(` / `confirm(` remaining in the analyst app (excluding `self-service/`, vendored Tinymce, and the LMS SCORM shim). Forms-with-`await showConfirm` audit confirmed every call site is now inside an `async` function. Future visual tweaks to the toast or confirm look-and-feel touch exactly one file each. |

| 442 | Forms             | Feature     | **Real form versioning &mdash; Save updates in place, Save as new version snapshots, Versions dropdown browses history.** Before: every regular Save bumped `version_number` with no actual snapshot, so "v3" was a counter not a thing you could revert to. After: a version *is* its own row in the chain. **Schema**: `forms.parent_form_id INT NULL` added &mdash; each row points back at its predecessor; the leaf (no children) is the editable current version, older rows are frozen. **`save_form.php`** no longer bumps `version_number`; just refreshes `modified_by/date`. Server-side check rejects in-place saves to non-leaf rows so a stale tab can't mutate history. **New APIs**: `create_version.php` (clones the current form + every `form_fields` row into a new chain entry whose `version_number = source + 1`; refuses to fork from a non-leaf) and `list_versions.php` (walks the chain back to root then forward, returns ordered rows with `is_current` flag &mdash; mirrors network-mapper's `list_versions.php` shape). `get_form.php` now returns `parent_form_id`, `version_number`, and an `is_leaf` boolean so the editor knows whether to enable Save. **Editor UI**: new toolbar v-pill (clickable; opens the Properties drawer), new Versions dropdown (lists the chain with the current row badged green; click any row to navigate to that version), new *Save as new version* button (offers to save in-progress changes first, then forks). When viewing a non-leaf row: orange read-only banner appears, Save is disabled with a tooltip explaining how to fork from the current version. **Two bugs fixed while in there**: (1) `saveForm()` now returns a success boolean so `createNewVersion()` can chain a save-before-fork. (2) The save payload only sent `options` for `dropdown` fields &mdash; the new `radio` / `checkboxes` types from #441 were losing their options on save. Switched to the shared `hasOptions()` helper. |
| 441 | Forms             | Feature     | **Four new form field types: email, number, radio buttons, checkboxes (multi-select).** Doubles the field type catalogue from four to eight. **email** uses `<input type="email">` for browser-native format validation (and `filter_var FILTER_VALIDATE_EMAIL` server-side). **number** uses `<input type="number">` to reject letters, plus `is_numeric` server-side. **radio** is a small visible group of mutually-exclusive options (good for 2-5 choices), distinct from `dropdown` which stays collapsed (good for 6+). **checkboxes** (plural) is a multi-select list &mdash; semantically different from the existing `checkbox` (singular yes/no toggle for consent flags), so both stay around. **Touch points**: badges + colours in `forms.css`; add-field menu + `renderFields` (now uses a shared `hasOptions()` helper) + `typeName()` + preview switch in both editors (`forms/edit/index.php` and the inline editor in `forms/index.php` for parity); render markup + per-type value collection in `forms/fill.php` (multi-select values JSON-encoded before submit); per-type required-empty checks + format validation in `submit_form.php`; comma-joined display + bullet list in detail view + CSV export handling for multi-select in `forms/submissions.php`; expanded *FIELD TYPES* + format-rules + sanitiser allow-list in `ai_generate.php` so AI Assist picks the right type for "email address" / "how many days" / "tick all that apply" prompts. **Storage**: multi-select values stored as a JSON-encoded array string in `form_submission_data.field_value` (no schema change &mdash; the column was already TEXT-shaped). All existing single-`checkbox`, `dropdown`, `text`, `textarea` fields untouched. |

| 424 | Morning checks    | Improvement | **Statuses fully normalised &mdash; results now FK on `StatusID` (was label-string-only), with a guided normalisation tool for any orphan data.** Follow-up to #421 / #422. The previous schema stored the label string in `morningChecks_Results.Status` and looked up colour / requires-notes by matching the string &mdash; pragmatic for the upgrade story but not actually normalised. This change goes properly normalised. **Schema**: added `StatusID INT NULL` to `morningChecks_Results` with FK `fk_results_status` to `morningChecks_Statuses (StatusID) ON DELETE SET NULL`. `Status VARCHAR(50)` widened to nullable &mdash; kept as a label snapshot for orphan rows (where StatusID is NULL because the source row was deleted or no match was found at migration time). **Migration** runs once via `db_verify.php`: relaxes `Status` to NULL, backfills `StatusID` from the existing label string (`UPDATE r JOIN s ON s.Label = r.Status SET r.StatusID = s.StatusID WHERE r.StatusID IS NULL`), then adds the FK constraint. For a vanilla install with the seeded Green/Amber/Red labels, 100% of historical rows backfill cleanly &mdash; zero orphans, no admin action needed. **Reads are now joined**: `get_todays_checks.php` LEFT JOINs the statuses table for label/colour/requires-notes (with an `IsOrphan` flag when StatusID is NULL but the Status snapshot is set); `get_chart_data.php` INNER JOINs on `StatusID` and groups by it (orphans excluded from the chart until remapped). **Writes carry the FK**: `save_check_result.php` now takes `statusId` instead of `status` (the dashboard sends the StatusID from the button it clicked), validates against the table, writes `StatusID` and sets `Status = NULL`. The dashboard's notes-modal hidden input changed from `modalStatusValue` to `modalStatusId`. **Deletes preserve labels for orphans**: `delete_status.php` now snapshots the about-to-be-deleted Label into `morningChecks_Results.Status` for any referencing row before deleting, all in one transaction &mdash; the FK SET NULL clears `StatusID` but the label survives so the normalisation tool can show what the orphan used to be. **Two new APIs**: `get_status_orphans.php` (distinct orphan labels with row counts &mdash; drives both the dashboard banner and the settings tool) and `normalise_status.php` (transactional bulk-map `{label, statusId}` pairs to set `StatusID` and clear `Status` on all matching orphan rows). **Dashboard**: shows a yellow warning banner with a link to Settings → Statuses when any orphans exist; per-row orphan badge in the status column when a check's most recent result is orphaned. **Settings → Statuses tab**: new highlighted normalisation section appears beneath the statuses table only when orphans exist &mdash; one row per distinct orphan label with count + a dropdown of active statuses + per-row *Map* button + *Map all* shortcut. **Cleanup**: `save_status.php`'s former rename-cascade `UPDATE morningChecks_Results SET Status = ? WHERE Status = ?` is gone (with the JOIN at read time, label changes propagate automatically; the old cascade would have wrongly claimed orphan rows that happened to share the old label). |

| 417 | Morning checks    | Improvement | **Chart expand/collapse now slides smoothly instead of snapping.** Replaced the old `display: none / block` toggle (which can't animate) with a `.collapsed` class that drops the chart-container's height + top/bottom padding + opacity to 0, all transitioning over 250ms. Chart-footer's `min-height: 40px` keeps the chevron visible at the end of the slide. **Two gotchas handled in JS**: (1) the inline `style.height` set by `applyChartHeightFromPct` would beat the collapsed class's `height: 0`, so the rule uses `!important` &mdash; the only reasonable place to use it given inline styles always win otherwise. (2) On expand, we update the target inline height first (so the transition has a valid end value if the window was resized while collapsed) but skip the immediate `chartInstance.resize()` call &mdash; the canvas parent is still 0px tall when the call would fire. A 280ms `setTimeout` (just after the transition lands) calls `chartInstance.resize()` so Chart.js redraws at the new canvas size. Divider visibility still toggles instantly with the class change so it doesn't sit half-shown during the slide. |

| 398 | Change management | Improvement | **Change form pairs half-width fields automatically &mdash; dropdowns and short inputs go 2-per-row, textareas / composites take the full row.** Follow-up to #397. The post-refactor form had every field stacked one-per-row, which wasted horizontal space on the dropdown-heavy *General* and *Schedule* sections. **Mechanism**: added a `width` property (`'half'` or `'full'`) to every entry in the shared `_field_catalogue.php`. Width is fixed per field type (dropdowns + datetime pickers + short text are `half`; textareas, composite widgets like CAB and risk-scoring, and headline fields like *Title* are `full`) so moving a field to a different section keeps its width. **Rendering**: `refreshFormLayout()` stamps `data-width` onto each `.cm-field-wrap` after positioning it; the change-management CSS turns `.cm-form-section` into a `display: flex; flex-wrap: wrap` row, with `half` wraps sized at `calc(50% - 10px)` and `full` wraps at 100% &mdash; pairing emerges automatically from layout order, no per-row container needed. **Orphan handling**: a `half` field whose neighbour isn't also `half` (i.e. it's between two fulls, or trailing at the end of a section) would leave awkward whitespace next to it. JS walks each section after placement and adds `.cm-field-half-orphan` to those, which stretches them back to full width. Determined by **adjacency in display order**, so reordering in Form Fields settings is what controls the pairing &mdash; admins can put two halves next to each other to pair them, or place a full between two halves to break them apart. **Also**: APIs (`get_field_layout`, `save_field_layout`) now return `width` alongside `label` per field; first-visible section gets a `.cm-form-section--first` class so its heading drops the top border / padding regardless of which section ended up first after reordering (replaces the old hardcoded inline `style="margin-top:0;..."` on the General-info heading); removed the matching dead inline style from `change-management/index.php`. | 397 | Change management | Feature     | **Form Fields settings now manages sections too &mdash; add / rename / reorder / delete sections, drag fields between them, auto-saves, and the change form reflects everything live.** The Form Fields tab used to be a flat list of *"show this field on the change form: yes / no"* checkboxes against a hardcoded *General / People / Schedule / Details / Attachments* section set. **Now**: full UI for managing the sections themselves &mdash; an *Add section* button at the top, each section rendered as its own card with a drag handle (reorder by drag), a *Rename* / *Delete* link, and the fields inside it shown as drag-handle rows with a *Visible* toggle. The only confirmation prompt is on section *Delete* and it tells you how many fields you'll be re-homing (you have to pick a destination section before the delete commits, so fields are never orphaned). **Unplaced fields** (catalogue keys that aren't in any section yet, e.g. after a future field-catalogue addition) surface as their own row under the section list so an admin can drag them into place. **Schema**: two new tables &mdash; `change_field_sections` (`id`, `name`, `display_order`) and `change_field_layout` (`field_key`, `section_id`, `display_order`, `is_visible`, unique key on `field_key`, FK to `change_field_sections` with `ON DELETE CASCADE`). It reorders the section blocks to match `section.display_order`, renames each heading from `section.name`, moves each `.cm-field-wrap` into the section its layout row points at, hides invisible fields, and hides any section that ends up with no visible content. Replaces the old `applyFieldVisibility()` / `SECTION_FIELDS` hardcoded map &mdash; the form is now fully data-driven. **v1 limitation noted in code**: the six rich-text tabs (Description / Reason / Risk / Test plan / Rollback / PIR) share a single anchored widget rather than being individually movable; the widget hosts itself under whichever section contains the first visible rich-text field, and the per-tab `is_visible` flags still hide individual tabs (with auto-switch to the next visible tab if the active one is hidden). | 389 | System            | Improvement | **Codebase-wide PHP session-locking sweep: every read-only API endpoint now releases the session lock immediately.** Follow-up to #388, which fixed the assets-settings 4.5s &rarr; 0.75s slowdown on six endpoints. Sweep of `api/` &mdash; **435 endpoints** changed from `session_start()` to `session_start(['read_and_close' => true])`, so any page firing concurrent AJAX (dashboards, asset table view, every settings page, the tickets inbox folder loads, the calendar, the rota, the help pages' embedded charts, etc.) now runs those requests in actual parallel instead of queueing behind PHP's default exclusive `flock` on the session file. **Skipped (deliberately)**: 9 files that mutate `$_SESSION` mid-request and need the lock to write safely &mdash; the analyst-side MFA + password-change flow (`api/myaccount/change_password.php`, `setup_mfa.php`, `verify_login_otp.php`, `verify_mfa.php`), the self-service portal auth flow (`api/self-service/login.php`, `register.php`, `update_profile.php`, `verify_login_otp.php`), and `api/system/save_analyst_modules.php`. Identification was mechanical &mdash; grep for `$_SESSION[...] = ` / `session_destroy` / `session_regenerate` / `session_unset` / `unset($_SESSION` &mdash; so anything not in that list was treated as read-only and safe to flip. Mechanism: `read_and_close` opens the session, populates `$_SESSION` for the auth-check (still works because the read happened before the close), then releases the file lock so subsequent requests in the same browser tab don't queue. Single-line change per file, no behavioural diffs for non-auth endpoints. |

| 383 | Assets            | Feature     | **Full-screen table view for the Assets module, with Excel-style filters, sortable / reorderable / hideable columns, CSV + PDF export, and per-analyst persistence.** New `asset-management/table.php` reachable from a new *Table* button in the assets module nav (between Assets and Dashboard). Loads all assets once on open and runs all interactions client-side &mdash; we deliberately chose client-side over server-side AJAX after debating it: at FreeITSM's realistic scale (< 10k assets per install), instant filter/sort/search beats round-trips per keystroke, and the Excel-style per-column distinct-values filter is much cleaner against an in-memory dataset. If a customer ever lands with 20k+ assets we'll add a server-side mode then, triggered automatically by row count rather than as a user-facing toggle. **What's there**: click any column header to sort (asc/desc cycle); the funnel icon on each header opens a tickbox dropdown of every distinct value currently in that column (counts per value, narrows to other active filters like Excel, has its own search box for long lists, *Select all* / *Clear* shortcuts); a global search across all visible columns; a *Columns* drawer to show/hide columns and drag them into the order you want; *Reset* to clear filters + search + sort in one click. Drag-reorder also works directly on the table headers. **Exports**: *CSV* (UTF-8 with BOM so Excel opens it cleanly, current visible columns + current filtered/sorted rows, escaped properly for embedded commas/quotes/newlines); *PDF* via jsPDF + autotable (landscape A4, blue header band, the company logo on the top left, "{visible} of {total} — {timestamp}" subhead, selectable text rather than a rasterised screenshot &mdash; same library + approach the morning-checks module uses). **Persistence**: visible columns, column order and sort direction save to `user_preferences` (key `asset_table_v1`) and survive across browsers / devices for each analyst. Search and active filters are deliberately transient session state. **Extensibility**: the entire feature set is driven by a single `COLUMNS` catalogue at the top of `assets/js/asset-table.js` &mdash; adding a future column is two lines (append to that array, ensure `get_assets.php` returns the field) and sort, filter, search, CSV and PDF all pick it up automatically. **DB**: bumped `user_preferences.preference_value` from `VARCHAR(500)` to `TEXT` (in `freeitsm.sql` + a one-off idempotent `ALTER TABLE` in `db_verify.php`) so config blobs don't constrain future column growth; raised the cap in `api/system/set_user_preference.php` to 60 KB. Three reads-from-the-existing-stack pieces reused: `api/assets/get_assets.php` (no API changes needed; already returns every field the table needs), `get_user_preference.php` / `set_user_preference.php` (the generic key-value preference endpoints that already existed), and the morning-checks PDF export pattern. |

| 365 | Tickets           | Feature     | **CSAT &mdash; customer satisfaction surveys on ticket closure.** Auto-survey when a ticket transitions into any closed status (or manual-only via a *Request feedback* button if you'd rather keep the analyst in the loop). Tokens are matched against the DB row, not parsed/decoded &mdash; even a database leak of `token` alone can't be replayed against a different install. Survey URL pattern is `/csat.php?token=...`; the landing page refuses already-responded tokens (one-shot only) and shows generic *"link not valid"* on misses so it doesn't leak which tokens exist. **Public landing page** (`csat.php`) &mdash; deliberately gorgeous, full-bleed gradient, branded thanks-screen on submit, no analyst chrome. Failure is swallowed and logged so a buggy CSAT template can't break ticket close. **Schema** &mdash; new `ticket_recordings`-style `ticket_recordings`... actually no, new `ticket_csat_responses` table (`id, ticket_id, token UNIQUE, sent_datetime, responded_datetime, rating TINYINT, comment TEXT, analyst_id, created_at`) added to `freeitsm.sql` and the `db_verify.php` `$schema` array plus the post-schema FK/index loop. | 362 | Self-Service      | Feature     | **Screen recordings &mdash; end users can record their screen straight from the new-ticket form, no plugins or third-party tools required.** Click *Record screen* on `self-service/new-ticket.php` to open an inline capture panel. The user picks whether to include microphone audio (off by default for privacy; checkbox sits above the Start button) then clicks **Start**, picks a tab/window/whole-screen from the browser's native picker, narrates and demonstrates the issue, and clicks **Stop** (or the browser's own "Stop sharing" bar). A preview `<video>` appears inline so they can re-record if they mucked it up, or hit *Use this* to upload. Hard 5-minute cap with a live `0:00` countdown next to the Stop button. **Format negotiation** &mdash; the capture probes `MediaRecorder.isTypeSupported()` for, in order, `video/mp4; codecs=avc1` (modern Chrome/Edge 134+ produces real MP4/H.264 in-browser), then `video/webm; codecs=vp9,opus`, falling all the way back to plain `video/webm`. Browser produces the best available format; the analyst's `<video>` element plays either, so cross-browser is invisible. **No DB blobs &mdash; files on disk only.** Uploads land in `recordings/pending/{uuid}.{ext}` (multipart POST to `api/self-service/upload_recording.php`, 50MB cap, MIME whitelist plus magic-byte sniff fallback so a browser sending `video/x-matroska` doesn't crash the upload). Server returns a `recording_id`; the new-ticket form holds it in memory alongside file attachments and posts the array of `recording_ids` to `create_ticket.php` on submit. The ticket-create flow then **claims** each pending row by setting `ticket_id` and `rename()`ing the file from `recordings/pending/` to `recordings/{ticket_id}/` &mdash; rename failures are logged but the DB row is still claimed so analysts can see what's broken. **Schema** &mdash; new `ticket_recordings` table (`id, ticket_id NULL, recorded_by_user_id NULL, filename, original_filename, content_type, file_path, file_size, duration_seconds, has_audio, created_at`) with FKs to `tickets` (ON DELETE CASCADE) and `users` (ON DELETE SET NULL) added to `freeitsm.sql` and the `db_verify.php` `$schema` + post-schema FK loop. **Streaming** &mdash; `api/self-service/get_recording.php` does dual auth (analyst session OR the ticket owner) and supports HTTP `Range` requests, so the `<video>` element can seek without downloading the entire file first. **Display** &mdash; on the self-service ticket detail page, recordings render as full-width `<video controls>` cards in a *Screen recordings* section above the conversation. In the analyst's inbox reading pane, they show as a horizontal-scrolling strip between the email header and the action toolbar (320px-wide cards, 200px max height, with filename / size / duration / "with audio" meta line beneath each). **iOS Safari has no `getDisplayMedia` support at all** &mdash; the Record button is hidden entirely (`navigator.mediaDevices.getDisplayMedia` probe on DOM-ready) on those browsers, so mobile users just don't see the option rather than getting a confusing error. **Recordings folder** &mdash; new top-level `recordings/` directory, gitignored except for an `.htaccess` Deny-all that blocks direct web access (the same pattern `contracts/rfp-builder/uploads/` uses); all serving goes via the streaming endpoint with proper auth. | 356 | Workflows         | Feature     | **Stage 4 (Tier 1 + Tier 2) &mdash; seven real action handlers, variable substitution, and a per-action form UI replacing the JSON textarea.** Until this commit the engine had a single action handler (`log_message`) which just wrote into the audit log &mdash; workflows could detect events and evaluate conditions, but couldn't actually *do* anything. **Seven new handlers** ship in `workflow/includes/engine.php`: **Tier 1 (single-module ticket actions)** &mdash; `set_ticket_status` (changes a ticket's status, auto-stamping / clearing `closed_datetime` when the new status's `is_closed` flag flips), `set_ticket_priority` (sets `priority_id`), `assign_ticket` (sets `assigned_analyst_id` AND `owner_id` so the right-pane Owner field stays in sync &mdash; mirrors the explicit-analyst branch of `assign_ticket.php`), `add_ticket_note` (writes a *Workflow Note* row to `ticket_audit` with `analyst_id = NULL` so the UI can render workflow-generated notes distinctly). **Tier 2 (cross-module)** &mdash; `send_email` (reuses every helper in `includes/template_email.php` &mdash; mailbox lookup, token refresh, Graph / Gmail dispatch, `templateSaveSentEmail` &mdash; but with ad-hoc subject + body rather than a stored template; defaults the recipient to the ticket's requester email when `to` is blank; builds the same `[SDREF:XXX-NNN-NNNNN] …` subject and reply-marker HTML body the rest of the app uses for threading), `create_task` (inserts into `tasks` with the same is_default fallback for status/priority and the same `MAX(board_position) + 1` calculation as `api/tasks/save.php`; auto-links the source ticket via `ticket_id`), `create_ticket` (full transactional flow mirroring `api/tickets/create_ticket.php` &mdash; upserts the user row by email, generates a unique `XXX-NNN-NNNNN` number, inserts the ticket, creates the initial *Manual*-direction email entry so the new ticket appears in the inbox like a manually-created one, writes a *Ticket Created* audit row attributed to the workflow). Every handler validates required args and throws on invalid lookups (engine catches the exception and marks the step *failed* in the step log without breaking subsequent steps). **Variable substitution** &mdash; new `renderTemplate($tmpl, $payload)` private helper expands `{{path.to.field}}` placeholders against the dispatch payload via dot-notation, so `subject: "Ticket {{ticket.id}} closed"` works. All free-text args run through this; arrays render as JSON to avoid PHP's surprising `Array` default. Two thin convenience helpers (`argString`, `argInt`) wrap it so handlers stay readable. **Richer action catalogue** &mdash; `availableActions()` now returns per-arg specs (`type`, `label`, `required`, `default`, `supports_vars`, `lookup`) rather than the old `name => 'string'` shorthand. The editor uses these to build a labelled form per action type with the right widget per arg: text input / textarea / number input / checkbox / lookup `<select>` (sourced from `availableActionLookup($key)` which reuses the same `FIELD_LOOKUP_TABLES` const that powers condition value dropdowns &mdash; one source of truth for "what are the active analysts / statuses / priorities"). Free-text args that support variables show an inline hint *"Supports variables like {{ticket.id}}…"* underneath. **Per-action canvas snippet** &mdash; the action node on the canvas now shows the most salient configured arg (e.g. *"&rarr; Critical"* for set_ticket_priority, the message for log_message, the subject for send_email / create_ticket) instead of a generic action label, so the diagram is glanceable. **AI co-author updated** &mdash; the system prompt's action catalogue is rebuilt as a per-arg bullet list with type / required / default / supports_vars annotations, plus the first 8 id=label pairs for any lookup arg's table so the AI can pick real ids. The "only `log_message` is implemented today" caveat is gone; new prompt rules cover `{{vars}}` (prefer `{{ticket.id}}` to a literal id so the workflow operates on whichever ticket triggered it) and lookup-id-as-string conventions. Catalogue lookup endpoints (status, priority, analyst, department, ticket_type, task_status, task_priority) exposed via `availableActionLookup($key)`. Old `updateActionArgsFromDetail` JSON-textarea handler removed from `WFE` exports along with the textarea itself. `workflow-editor.js` &rarr; `?v=8`. Stage 4 *Tier 3* (Microsoft Graph actions &mdash; `graph_add_to_group`, `graph_assign_license`, `graph_disable_user`) and Stage 6 (operational polish, dry-run, starter recipes, versioning) remain. |
| 354 | Workflows         | Feature     | **Stage 5 (Tickets portion) &mdash; host module trigger wiring: tickets now fire workflow events for real.** Until this commit the engine could be exercised only via the editor's *Test fire* button; the four `ticket.*` triggers in `WorkflowEngine::availableTriggers()` were declared but never dispatched from the host module's save flow, so an active workflow with *trigger = priority changed, condition = is Critical* did nothing when a real ticket was actually marked Critical. **`api/tickets/assign_ticket.php`** &mdash; pre-update state fetch extended to also capture `status_id` and `priority_id` (alongside the existing `assigned_analyst_id` / `status name` / `is_closed`); after the successful `UPDATE` and the existing template-email block, a defensive try/catch issues three potential dispatches: **`ticket.status_changed`** when `newStatusId !== oldStatusId`, **`ticket.priority_changed`** when the priority was sent and `newPriorityId !== oldPriorityId`, and **`ticket.assigned`** when the new analyst differs from the old. Payloads match the field hints in `WorkflowEngine::availableFields()` &mdash; e.g. priority_changed sends `{ticket: {id, status_id, assigned_analyst_id}, old_priority_id, new_priority_id}` so conditions on either the new value or the previous one work as documented. **`api/tickets/create_ticket.php`** &mdash; after `$conn->commit()` and the success response, reads back the resolved `status_id` / `priority_id` (the INSERT uses name-based subselects so the ids aren't known client-side) and dispatches **`ticket.created`** with the full ticket-shape payload: id, subject, priority_id, status_id, department_id, type_id, assigned_analyst_id, created_by, requester_email. **Belt-and-braces error handling:** `WorkflowEngine::dispatch()` already swallows its own errors and logs to `workflow_executions`, but each call site is also wrapped in a try/catch logging to `error_log()` so an engine-layer outage (e.g. workflow table missing, db connection blip) can never bubble out and break the ticket save response that's already been echoed to the client. **Net effect:** an active workflow with trigger *ticket.priority_changed* and condition *new_priority_id is one of: Critical* fires the moment a user changes a ticket's priority to Critical from the right-click menu or the toolbar dropdown &mdash; a row appears in `workflow_executions` with the full `step_log` and the workflow's `last_run_*` columns update. Stages 4 (real action handlers: set_ticket_status, send_email, create_task, Graph actions) and 6 (operational polish, dry-run, Watchtower integration, starter recipes, workflow versioning) still to come; this commit closes the *can-actually-fire-from-real-events* loop for the Tickets module. |

| 348 | Workflows         | Improvement | **Operator dropdown is filtered by field type so `gt`/`lt` doesn't appear on varchars and `contains` doesn't appear on numeric ids.** Previously the free-text branch of the operator dropdown offered the entire catalogue regardless of field, so a user could pick `subject &gt; "foo"` and get MariaDB's lexicographic string comparison &mdash; technically valid SQL, almost certainly not what they meant. Engine gained a `fieldType($fieldPath)` helper backed by a `FIELD_TYPES` const that classifies each non-lookup field as `numeric` or `text` (with a sensible default for unrecognised paths: anything ending in `.id` is numeric, everything else is text). New `operatorsForFieldType($type)` returns the valid op slugs per type &mdash; *numeric*: equals/not_equals/in/not_in/gt/lt/is_empty/is_not_empty; *text*: equals/not_equals/in/not_in/contains/not_contains/is_empty/is_not_empty (note no `gt`/`lt` for text and no `contains` for numeric). Editor exports `window.WF_FIELD_TYPES` and `rebuildOperatorDropdown()` uses it to build the right operator list; if a saved workflow had an invalid op for the field (e.g. an old `subject gt "foo"`), it falls back to a sane default (`equals` for free-text, `in` for lookup) so the dropdown isn't blank. AI co-author updated: prompt now annotates every field with its type (e.g. *"ticket.subject (text)"*, *"ticket.id (numeric)"*, *"ticket.priority_id (lookup) [1=Low, ...]"*) and explicitly tells the AI which ops are valid per type so it can't propose nonsense. Server-side validator drops type-mismatched conditions with a warning rather than passing them through. `workflow-editor.js` &rarr; `?v=6`. |
| 346 | Workflows         | Feature     | **Condition panel resolves normalised ids to real values + adds OR-semantics multi-select.** Two related upgrades to make conditions friendly. **(1) Lookup-table awareness.** Normalised id fields like `ticket.priority_id`, `ticket.status_id`, `ticket.department_id`, `ticket.type_id`, `ticket.assigned_analyst_id`, `task.priority_id`, etc. now drive a dropdown of *real* values pulled from the joined table (`ticket_priorities`, `ticket_statuses`, `departments`, `ticket_types`, `analysts`, `teams`, `forms`, `task_priorities`, `task_statuses`) instead of asking the user to type opaque ids. The mapping lives in a private `FIELD_LOOKUP_TABLES` const on `WorkflowEngine`; a new `WorkflowEngine::availableValuesForField($fieldPath)` queries the relevant table (with `is_active = 1` and `display_order, name` ordering where appropriate) and returns `[{id, label}, ...]` or `null` for free-text fields. Defensive try/catch returns null if the lookup table doesn't exist (older installs that haven't migrated) so the editor falls back to a plain text input. **(2) Two new operators &mdash; `in` / `not_in` &mdash; for OR semantics.** *"Priority is Critical OR High"* used to require two separate conditions joined by AND, which doesn't actually express OR; now it's a single condition with `op = "in"` and `value = ["4", "3"]`. The condition panel's value control adapts based on (field has lookup) &times; (op): single dropdown for lookup + equals/not_equals, checkbox list for lookup + in/not_in (with the lookup's id shown in muted text next to each label), free-text input for non-lookup fields, comma-separated for non-lookup + in/not_in, and hidden for is_empty / is_not_empty. Canvas node preview now resolves ids to labels (e.g. *"priority_id is one of: Critical, High"* instead of *"priority_id in 4, 3"*) so the diagram stays glanceable. Engine evaluator gained `in` / `not_in` cases backed by a new `value_in_list()` helper that's tolerant on input shape (array, comma-separated string, or scalar). **AI co-author updated to know about lookups + the new ops.** `api/workflow/ai_compose.php`'s system prompt now annotates each lookup field with its id&rarr;label map (e.g. *"ticket.priority_id [1=Low, 2=Normal, 3=High, 4=Critical]"*) so the AI can pick the right id from plain English (*"Critical or High priority"* &rarr; `op:"in", value:["4","3"]`). The prompt explains value-shape-per-op explicitly. Server-side validator coerces value to the right shape for the op (array for in/not_in, string otherwise) rather than dropping mismatched conditions. New i18n entries for `op.in` / `op.not_in`. `workflow-editor.js` &rarr; `?v=4`. |

| 335 | Process Mapper    | Improvement | **Step detail panel no longer flashes open mid-drag.** Clicking a step used to call `showDetailForStep()` on mousedown, which meant any time you grabbed a step to drag it the panel slid in for a split second before sliding back out (or worse, stayed open with stale data if a re-render happened mid-drag). Deferred the panel show to `onDocMouseUp`'s click-without-drag branch &mdash; if `dragging.moved` is false at mouseup, the panel opens then; if the user actually dragged, the panel stays exactly as it was. Ctrl+click selection-toggle still opens the panel immediately because that path doesn't start a drag. `process-mapper.js` &rarr; `?v=9`. |
| 334 | Process Mapper    | Feature     | **Step right-click menu expanded with eight new actions, URL links per step, and sticky-note annotations.** Right-clicking a step now offers four grouped sections of actions. **Group 1 (per-step)**: *Edit label* (alias for double-click inline rename), *Add note* (drops a sticky-note annotation tethered to the step), *Link to URL…* (prompt-set a link target — validated to `http(s)://` only — adds a small chain-link badge to the step's top-right corner that opens in a new tab when clicked, with mousedown/click `stopPropagation()` so the badge doesn't kick off a step drag). **Group 2 (type + connectors)**: existing *Create new…* and *Change to…* submenus, *Connect to…* (existing click-to-connect mode), new *Reverse connection…* submenu listing every incident connector with an arrow showing direction and the other end's label (greyed when the step has no connectors), new *Delete all connections* (confirms then removes every edge incident to the step). **Group 3 (clipboard)**: full *Cut / Copy / Paste* with file-manager semantics — Cut visually fades the source via `.pm-step.is-cut` and removes the original only when Paste happens (the cut+paste pair behaves like a move); Copy keeps the clipboard live so it can be pasted multiple times; Paste drops the new step at the right-click cursor position (`ctxRightClickPos` stashed by `onStepContextMenu`); Escape un-fades a pending cut. | 318 | Tasks             | Feature     | **Search box on the board and list views.** A search field at the top of the Tasks sidebar filters the board and list as you type &mdash; matching on task title and (plain-text) description. Multi-word queries are AND-matched, so "login fix" matches a task titled "Fix the login bug". Filtering is entirely client-side on the already-loaded task set (no server round-trip), so it's instant; the searchable text for each task is pre-computed once per load. The board's per-column counts reflect the matches while a search is active, and a clear (&times;) button resets it. The query persists across the Board/List toggle and across My/All/Team/Analyst filter changes. `tasks.js` bumped to `?v=5`, `tasks.css` to `?v=7`. |
| 319 | Tasks             | Improvement | **Board now shows one column per status.** The board previously had three hardcoded columns (To Do / In Progress / Done), so tasks in any other status &mdash; Blocked, Cancelled, or any custom status &mdash; silently had no column and vanished from the board. The board now generates its columns from the active statuses in Settings &rarr; Statuses, in `display_order`, each headed with the status's colour dot; nothing can fall off the board. Quick-add, drag-and-drop reordering and per-column counts all work per generated column. The detail panel's Status and Priority dropdowns are now also built from the configured lookups (instead of a hardcoded four each), and the List view's status pill is tinted with the status's own colour so custom statuses render consistently. Practical upside: creating a custom status (e.g. an "Icebox" or "Blue Sky" parking-lot for someday-maybe ideas) now simply gives you a new board column &mdash; no separate "non-status column" concept needed. `tasks.js` bumped to `?v=6`, `tasks.css` to `?v=8`. |
| 321 | Tasks             | Feature     | **Drag board columns to reorder them.** A board column header is now a drag handle &mdash; drag it left/right and the columns reshuffle live; on drop the new order is persisted by rewriting each status's `display_order` (new `api/tasks/reorder_task_statuses.php` endpoint). It's the same `display_order` the Settings &rarr; Statuses tab edits, so the two stay in sync, and the calendar's status legend / context-menu / dropdown ordering follow too. The column header gets a grab cursor; the dragged column dims while moving. Card drag-and-drop is unaffected (cards drag from the card body, columns from the header; the + button is excluded as a handle). `tasks.js` bumped to `?v=8`, `tasks.css` to `?v=10`. |
| 320 | Tasks             | Feature     | **Task tags.** Tasks can now carry any number of free-form labels for cross-cutting themes &mdash; e.g. Security, ISO, Environment (seeded as defaults). Two new tables: `task_tags` (name, colour, order) and a `task_tag_map` many-to-many junction with `ON DELETE CASCADE` both ways; both added to `freeitsm.sql` and `db_verify.php` (schema, composite-PK handling, FKs and seed) so existing installs auto-migrate. New **Settings &rarr; Tags** tab manages the tag vocabulary (reusing the Statuses/Priorities lookup table + modal, extended with `hasDefault`/`hasActive` flags so tags show just Name/Colour/Order) and carries the display options. **Five toggles** govern tagging per-install: *Allow new tags from a task* (managed vs. inline-create &mdash; the free-form/hybrid distinction collapsed to one switch since with colours they're the same thing), plus four surface toggles &mdash; *Card chips*, *Sidebar filter*, *Search matching*, *Calendar &amp; timeline*. The detail panel gains a tag picker (type-to-filter combobox with removable chips, and inline create when allowed); board/list cards show coloured tag chips; the sidebar gains a tag filter; the search box matches tag names; and the calendar/timeline show small tag dots on task bars &mdash; each honouring its surface toggle. ### 17 May 2026

| ID  | Module            | Type        | Description |

| 308 | Tickets           | Fix         | **SLA help page Example 2 (Estonia cross-timezone) options shown inconsistent margins**. User-caught: Options A and B both landed the SLA at the literal wire (consumption = target exactly), while Option C showed 30 min margin &mdash; making C look unfairly generous in comparison when really all three meet the SLA at the same level. Fix is consistent: bumped the raise time from 16:00 UK Friday to 16:30 UK Friday throughout the scenario, then picked reply times in each option that consume exactly 30 min of the 60 min target. **Option A (UK calendar)**: 30 min consumed Friday 16:30-17:00 UK, paused weekend, Estonia analyst replies 10:00 Estonia Mon (= 08:00 UK while UK calendar still paused) &mdash; consumption stays at 30 min, met with 30 min margin. Added a "any reply after 09:30 UK / 11:30 Estonia would breach" line to make the wire visible. **Option B (Estonia calendar)**: ticket arrives 18:30 Estonia Friday (after Estonia close), clock starts Mon 09:00 Estonia, analyst replies 09:30 Estonia (= 07:30 UK), 30 min consumed, met with 30 min margin. The wall-clock-vs-SLA gap is still in the prose (UK customer raised 16:30 Friday UK, replied 07:30 UK Monday). **Option C (overlap calendar)**: ticket raised 16:30 UK Friday (outside the overlap which closes 15:00 UK), reply at 11:30 Estonia Monday (= 09:30 UK, 30 min into the overlap reopening), 30 min consumed, met with 30 min margin. All three now show the same outcome with the same margin, so readers can compare the *qualitative* differences (who feels the pressure, who waits how long wall-clock) rather than being misled by quantitative artefacts of arbitrary example times. Four-paragraph edit; no schema or behaviour change. |
| 307 | Tickets           | Fix         | **SLA help page Example 1 maths wrong**. User caught a self-inflicted bug in the worked example I shipped in #306. Ticket raised Wed 16:30 with a 1h response target on a Mon-Fri 09:00-17:00 calendar: 30 min consumed Wed 16:30-17:00 + 30 min consumed Thu 09:00-09:30 = exactly 60 min = at the wire, not "with 30 min to spare". And a reply at Thu 10:00 would consume 30 + 60 = 90 min = 150% / breached by 30 min, not "exactly 100%". Kept the times (Thu 09:30 and Thu 10:00) and fixed the prose to match the correct maths &mdash; the breach scenario at Thu 10:00 is actually more useful for teaching than the "comfortable margin" version because it illustrates the easy-to-miss trap where an analyst arriving at 09:00 assumes they have the full hour, when 30 min has already been consumed the previous evening. Single-paragraph edit, no other changes. |

| 304 | Tickets           | Fix         | **`TypeError: t is not a function` when loading Email Templates tab in settings**. | 303 | Watchtower        | Feature     | **"Tickets paused too long" guardrail on the Watchtower dashboard**. Crossover between the Tickets/SLA pause-the-clock feature (#295/#298) and Watchtower's at-a-glance attention model. Catches the well-known ITIL antipattern of analysts parking tickets in "On Hold" / "Awaiting Vendor" to escape the SLA clock when they're stuck or busy &mdash; tickets sit indefinitely with the SLA showing as paused, customer experience suffers, but reporting looks fine because the SLA metric isn't tripping. Now the Tickets card on Watchtower shows an amber attention row whenever there are tickets currently in a paused-SLA status (any status with `pauses_sla = 1`) where the last status change was longer ago than the configured threshold (wall-clock hours). Threshold lives in `system_settings.watchtower_paused_too_long_hours` (default **24 hours** &mdash; allows overnight pauses but flags anything sitting through a full working day). Anchor for "how long has it been paused" is the latest `ticket_audit` row with `field_name = 'status'`; falls back to `tickets.created_datetime` if no status-change row exists (e.g. ticket has never moved off its default status). Single SQL query, no per-row PHP work &mdash; uses a correlated subquery joined to the audit table so it scales to thousands of tickets. The Tickets card's dot flips to amber if the count is > 0 (in addition to the existing urgent/unassigned triggers), so the entire dashboard's red/amber/green status reflects this new signal too. Doesn't change the SLA engine's pause behaviour or the cron worker &mdash; it's purely an "is anyone abusing this?" surveillance signal on top of the existing feature. Setting seeded by `db_verify.php` so existing installs pick it up on next verify. Configurable via SQL for v1 (`UPDATE system_settings SET setting_value = '8' WHERE setting_key = 'watchtower_paused_too_long_hours'` if you want a tighter 8-hour window for a managed-service team). A proper settings UI for this can come later if requested. |

| 301 | Tickets           | Improvement | **Rate limiting + per-run logging on the SLA breach-check cron**. Two follow-ups to #299 the user asked for. **(1) Rate limiting** &mdash; three layers, the first two HTTP-only, the third applied to CLI + HTTP equally: (a) the existing shared-secret token check (#299); (b) **per-IP failed-auth lockout** &mdash; >10 wrong-token attempts from the same IP in the past hour returns 429 for a full hour, defeating brute-force probing without needing fail2ban or similar; (c) **min interval between successful runs** &mdash; `sla_cron_min_interval_seconds` setting (default 30s, configurable in `system_settings`); even a valid-token request gets a 429 if it arrives sooner than that after the last successful run. Catches accidental double-scheduling, runaway loops, and post-token-leak abuse without affecting any reasonable schedule (5-min crons sit comfortably above 30s). **(2) Per-run logging** &mdash; new **`sla_cron_runs`** table with one row per invocation: `started_at` / `ended_at` / `duration_ms` / `invocation` (cli|http) / `client_ip` / `outcome` (ok / rate_limited / auth_failed / config_missing / error) / `sent_count` / `skipped_count` / `error_count` / `notes`. Indexed on `started_at` and `(client_ip, started_at)` so the rate-limit lookups stay O(log n). Logs both accepted *and* rejected runs &mdash; same source of truth for the rate-limit check + a security audit (you can see exactly when someone hit you with the wrong token and from where). Rows pruned automatically at the end of every run based on `sla_cron_log_retention_days` (default 30 days, configurable). Keeps the table tiny even at 1-minute cadence: 1440 rows/day &times; 30 days = ~43k rows, well within a single index page. **(3) Cron Activity panel in settings** &mdash; new section below Breach Notifications shows the last 20 invocations with colour-coded outcome pills (green=ok, amber=rate_limited, red=auth_failed/error), source (CLI / HTTP+IP), duration, and per-run counts. Refresh button reloads. Hover any row to see the full notes (sent items, error details). Powered by new `api/tickets/get_sla_cron_runs.php` endpoint. The header echoes the current `min_interval_seconds` + `retention_days` so admins see the active values without rooting around in `system_settings`. **Updates**: `database/freeitsm.sql` + `db_verify.php` schema + idempotent indexes + 2 new seeded settings (`sla_cron_min_interval_seconds`, `sla_cron_log_retention_days`); cron worker rewritten with `sla_cron_log_start` / `sla_cron_log_finish` helpers that wrap every code path including the early-exit rejects; `docs/sla-cron-setup.md` gains "Security layers" + "Tuning settings" sections + two new troubleshooting rows for the 429 cases. No cache buster bumps (no inbox.css/js changes). |

| 299 | Tickets           | Feature     | **SLA breach notifications &mdash; configurable per-department rules + cron worker (step 5 of `docs/sla.md` complete)**. Closes the SLA loop: until now the engine knew when tickets were approaching / past breach but only surfaced this passively in the reading pane + inbox pill. This adds the active push: emails fire to configured recipients whenever a ticket crosses the warning threshold (**potential** breach &mdash; `sla_warning_threshold_percent`, default 80%) or actually breaches (**actual**). **Schema** (two new tables): **`sla_notification_rules`** &mdash; one row per rule with `department_id` (NULL = default rule applied when no per-dept rule matches), `trigger_type` (warning / breach), `target_type` (response / resolution / both), four recipient fields covering all four use cases the user wanted (`notify_assignee` bool, `notify_department_teams` bool, `notify_analyst_id` FK, `notify_emails` TEXT for free-form comma/semicolon-separated lists), `is_active` toggle, audit cols. **`sla_notifications_sent`** &mdash; dedup log with UNIQUE on `(ticket_id, target_type, trigger_type)` so each combination fires at most once per ticket; cron worker checks this before sending. Walks open non-closed tickets (cap 2000 / run), pulls SLA state from the existing engine, decides which triggers apply (warning if `>= warning_threshold && < 100`, breach if breached &mdash; with catch-up logic so a missed warning still fires before its breach if cron was down), finds the most-specific matching rule via 4-tier resolution (per-dept-specific-target → per-dept-both → default-specific-target → default-both), resolves recipients (joining `department_teams` + `analyst_teams` to expand the "dept teams" checkbox into actual mailboxes), and sends via the ticket's originating mailbox using the existing `templateGetMailboxForTicket` / `templateSendViaGraph` / `gmailSendEmail` infrastructure (reuses OAuth tokens + refresh logic). HTTP form requires `?token=<value>` matching the `sla_cron_token` system setting (auto-seeded as `bin2hex(random_bytes(16))` on first verify so each install gets a unique secret); CLI skips the token check since filesystem perms already gate it. 120-second `set_time_limit` hard cap. | 297 | Tickets           | Feature     | **SLA engine + reading-pane panel** &mdash; steps 3 + 4 of the SLA plan (`docs/sla.md`). **`includes/sla.php`** is the engine: pure-PHP, compute-on-read, no stored counters. `sla_get_state(PDO $conn, int $ticket_id)` returns the full SLA state of a ticket &mdash; checks the global cutoff (`sla_enforce_from`), loads the priority + calendar (falling back to the default calendar if the priority doesn't have one set), walks the ticket's status-change audit history to build a "running vs. paused" timeline (using each status's `pauses_sla` flag), and intersects each running interval with the calendar's business hours via the standalone `sla_business_minutes()` function. **Business-hours intersection** walks day-by-day in the calendar's timezone, skips holidays + closed weekdays, and intersects the day's working window with the requested interval &mdash; ~50 lines, handles DST and timezones natively via `DateTimeImmutable` + `DateTimeZone`. Response SLA stops the clock at the first non-default status change (v1 simplification &mdash; the `sla_first_response_definition` setting is honoured by the engine API but all three options currently fall through to status-change detection; outbound-email detection deferred per `docs/sla.md`'s "Open questions"). Resolution SLA stops at `tickets.closed_datetime` or the first transition into a status with `is_closed = 1`. **New API endpoint**: `api/tickets/get_ticket_sla.php` &mdash; thin wrapper around the engine, called from the reading pane after `displayEmail()`. **SLA panel** in the reading pane: appears below the linked CMDB objects, above Time Entries. Shows Response + Resolution rows each with a coloured left border (green = on track / achieved, amber = warning threshold, red = breached), a colour-coded progress bar showing % elapsed, a status pill (*On track* / *Approaching breach* / *Breached* / *Achieved*), and the meta line (Target Xh Ym &middot; Elapsed Xh Ym &middot; Yh Zm remaining / Over by Xh Ym / Achieved in Xh Ym). Panel hides itself silently if SLA is disabled for the ticket (no global cutoff set, ticket pre-dates the cutoff, no priority, no SLA target on the priority, no calendar) &mdash; no "SLA disabled for this ticket" clutter for analysts. **Implementation plan progress**: step 3 (engine) + step 4 (reading-pane surfacing) done. | 295 | Tickets           | Feature     | **SLA module schema** &mdash; step 1 of the SLA implementation plan from `docs/sla.md`. | 291 | Tickets           | Fix         | **Buttons broken across all 18 languages on the tickets settings page after #290**. Self-inflicted: my replace_all swap used `old_string: '>Add</button>'` and `new_string: '<?php echo ... ?></button>'` &mdash; dropping the `>` that closes the opening `<button>` tag. Net effect was `<button class="add-btn" onclick="..."<?php echo ... ?></button>`, which leaves the opening tag malformed: PHP runs and emits the translated text, but the browser sees an unclosed-attribute mess and the button doesn't render as a clickable button at all (collapsing into the surrounding HTML). Same bug in 9 button-text patterns &mdash; the 4 bulk replaces (Add ×11, Save ×6, Cancel ×6, Close ×2) and 5 per-instance swaps (Logs, Check All, Test connection, Verify, Reset Password). Fix: replace_all again with `'<?php echo ... ?></button>'` → `'><?php echo ... ?></button>'` so the opening tag's closing `>` is restored. PHP lint clean. JS pagination Prev/Next swaps from the same PR were never affected because their old_string already included `">` which was preserved. The mistake would have been visible immediately in any browser smoke-test of the page &mdash; lesson: when bulk-replacing across tag boundaries, double-check the `<` and `>` are still balanced in the new string. |

| 283 | Tickets           | Fix         | **Email body still bleeding into CMDB / Time Entries panels after #282 — second layer of containment**. #282's DOMParser pass balanced unclosed tags but didn't stop two other escape routes: (a) `<style>` blocks inside the email applying global selectors (e.g. an Outlook footer block's stylesheet repositioning content with `position: absolute`); (b) absolutely-positioned descendants escaping their container because the wrapper wasn't a containing block. Ed's screenshot of MFG-151-13903 showed the "Did you find this email helpful?" grey box visually floating *over* the Time Entries section &mdash; a textbook positioning-escape symptom, not a tag-balance one. Two targeted fixes: **JS** &mdash; `safeEmailHtml()` now also strips `<style>`, `<script>`, `<link>`, `<base>`, `<meta>` tags from the parsed document before returning the serialised body. DOMParser already does this in a separate document context, so the stripped tags never touch the live DOM. **CSS** &mdash; `.email-body-content` and `.thread-message-body` get `contain: layout paint` (creates a containing block so absolutely-positioned descendants are positioned relative to the email box, not the page; clips painting at the box boundary) plus `overflow: hidden` (belt-and-braces for any layout-overflow that doesn't trigger `contain: paint`'s clipping). Together: HTML can't bleed (tag balance), CSS can't bleed (`<style>` stripped), and positioning can't bleed (containing block + paint clip). Cache busters bumped to `inbox.css?v=17` and `inbox.js?v=20`. |
| 282 | Tickets           | Fix         | **Malformed email bodies (unclosed tags) swallowed the CMDB / time-entries / notes panels below them**. Reported via ticket MFG-151-13903 where the email body ran straight into the operational sections at the bottom of the reading pane. Root cause: email HTML was interpolated raw into the reading pane via template literals (`<div class="email-body-content">${email.body_content}</div>` and the same for thread messages). When that HTML contains an unclosed tag &mdash; a `<div>` with no closing `</div>`, an open `<font>` running to end-of-message, half a `<table>` &mdash; the browser's HTML parser balances the unclosed tag at the end of its *parent* element rather than at the end of the email body. Net effect: the sibling containers that followed (`#cmdbObjectsContainer`, `#timeEntriesContainer`, `#notesContainer`) silently ended up nested *inside* the email body's runaway element, with all the visual chaos that implies. Server-side processing in `get_email_detail.php` only strips control characters; nothing balances tags. Fix is a one-helper `safeEmailHtml(html)` function in `inbox.js` that runs the email body through `DOMParser.parseFromString(html, 'text/html')` and returns `doc.body.innerHTML`. DOMParser invokes the same battle-tested HTML parser the browser uses for full page loads &mdash; it auto-balances any unclosed tags as it builds the parsed document's body, so the serialised output is well-formed and cannot bleed into sibling elements when assigned via innerHTML. Bonus security property: scripts in the parsed document don't execute (documented behaviour of DOMParser for `text/html`). Applied at both injection sites &mdash; the single-email body (`renderTicket`) and each message in the conversation thread (`loadCorrespondenceThread`). No CSS or DOM-structure changes needed because the tag balancing happens *before* the HTML hits the live DOM, which is the only point at which the bleed can actually occur. Cache buster bumped to `inbox.js?v=19`. |

Closing the modal refreshes the CMDB-objects section of the reading pane *only if* the affected ticket is the one currently open there, so the UI stays in sync without redundant re-renders. **Action 2 — Record time**: opens a modal with the same fields as the inline form (#279) plus a datetime-local picker so you can backdate (defaults to "now" in local time). Saves via the existing `api/tickets/save_time_entry.php`. Same reading-pane re-render gate &mdash; only refreshes the time-entries section if it's the currently-open ticket. Both modals reuse the standard `.modal` / `.modal-content` chrome (no new CSS for that part); new CSS limited to the `.ticket-context-menu` popover, the modal-scoped `.ctx-cmdb-results` list, and the result-row hover styling. No new API endpoints, no schema changes. Cache busters bumped to `inbox.css?v=16` and `inbox.js?v=18`. Out of scope for this first cut: keyboard navigation of the CMDB result list (mouse only), editing existing time entries, bulk multi-ticket selection (the "(s)" in the menu refers to linking multiple CMDB objects to one ticket in one session, not multi-ticket batch ops). |
| 279 | Tickets           | Feature     | **Time tracking against tickets**. | 277 | Tickets           | Fix         | **Pop-out mode trapped users in no-mans-land after F5 with no ticket selected**. The persistence introduced in #273 saved the popout preference to `localStorage` and an IIFE auto-applied `body.ticket-popout` on every page load. After an F5 the inbox starts with no ticket selected and the reading pane in its "Select a ticket" empty state &mdash; combine that with the popout class auto-applied from localStorage and the folder + email list panes were hidden, leaving the user with nothing actionable but the Exit pill (added in #274 as a band-aid). Tickets are loaded by AJAX so the URL never carries a ticket id; there's no native browser state to anchor the popout view to. **Real fix**: tie the popout class to the *actual* reading-pane state rather than a saved preference applied blind. New `syncPopoutToTicketState(hasTicket)` helper does the work: when called with `true` (a ticket has just rendered), it reads the localStorage pref and adds the class if set; when called with `false` (any empty / error state), it always strips the class. Wired in two places: at the end of `displayEmail()` (apply class once ticket markup is in the DOM), and at each of the four "no ticket loaded" branches in `selectEmail` and `loadTicketById` (strip class on error / not found). The on-load IIFE that applied the class blind is gone &mdash; an F5 now always lands in the default 3-column view, and the popout reapplies the moment the user picks a ticket. Deliberately doesn't strip on the transient loading state (`<div class="loading">`) so switching tickets mid-popout doesn't flicker 3-col → popout. Double-click handler simplified to just write the pref and call `selectEmail` &mdash; the render path does the class application, so timing is automatic. Cache buster bumped to `?v=13`. |

| 272 | Tasks             | Fix         | **Tasks Settings action icons still stacked vertically after #271's `white-space: nowrap` fix**. Real cause was different from the first diagnosis: the shared `assets/css/inbox.css` line 701 declares `.action-btn { display: flex; ... }` &mdash; which makes every `.action-btn` a *block-level* flex container, so two of them in the same `<td>` stack vertically (flex containers are block-level by default). `white-space: nowrap` on the parent has no effect because the children aren't inline. The page-local `.action-btn` rule at the top of `tasks/settings/index.php` overrode padding/border/colour but didn't reset `display`. Fix is a one-liner: `.actions-cell .action-btn { display: inline-flex; vertical-align: middle; }` — higher specificity (0,2,0) than the inbox.css rule (0,1,0) so it wins the cascade, and `inline-flex` keeps the icon-centring behaviour of flex while sitting inline like a button should. Kept #271's `white-space: nowrap` as belt-and-braces in case future content makes overflow possible. |

Continues the home/waffle i18n push (#261/#262) into the third major user-facing surface — the scheduled-tickets calendar view at `/tickets/calendar.php`. Mai 2026 um 14:30", ja-style 24-hour vs en-US AM/PM picked by the browser per locale). JS bridge wired via `window.translations = json_encode(I18n::exportForJs(['common', 'tickets']))` in the page `<head>`, then `<script src="../assets/js/i18n.js"></script>` exposes `window.t()` for calendar.js. **Translation conventions** honoured per locale: French / Spanish / Italian / Polish / Russian / Portuguese months and weekdays lower-cased per native orthography (`'monday' => 'lundi'`, `'january' => 'enero'`), German title-cased (`'monday' => 'Montag'`, `'january' => 'Januar'`), Indic locales in native scripts (Hindi `'जनवरी'`, Tamil `'ஜனவரி'`, Punjabi `'ਜਨਵਰੀ'` etc.), Brazilian Portuguese long-form weekdays (`segunda-feira` … `sexta-feira`). "N/A" preserved as the universal abbreviation across all locales since native equivalents would lose recognisability for power users. **calendar.js graceful fallback**: introduced a tiny `tr(key, params)` helper that checks `typeof window.t === 'function'` and returns the key verbatim if the i18n bridge isn't loaded — so legacy pages that include `calendar.js` without the bridge keep rendering (in English) rather than throwing a ReferenceError. **Out of scope**: the top-level `calendar/` module (separate from `tickets/calendar.php`) and the rota / dashboard / users / settings sub-pages of Tickets are still untranslated; this PR establishes the calendar primitive vocabulary that those pages will reuse when they come up. |
| 262 | Project           | Fix         | **Home screen ignored the user's selected language (still rendered English)** even after #261 wired up the translations. Root cause: `I18n::initFromSession()` reads the analyst's `interface_language` preference from the database, but it gates the lookup on `function_exists('connectToDatabase')` so it stays safe to call before `includes/functions.php` is loaded. #261 bootstrapped i18n from `includes/waffle-menu.php` — which works for `tickets/` and `process-mapper/` because their index pages explicitly require `functions.php` before the header runs, but breaks for `index.php` (and any other page going straight from `config.php` to the waffle include) because `config.php` doesn't transitively pull in `functions.php`. With `connectToDatabase` undefined at init time, the DB branch was silently skipped and the locale resolution fell through to `Accept-Language` → English regardless of what the user had picked in System → Preferences. The waffle menu *did* translate when viewed from a Tickets / Process Mapper page (where their own init had already loaded the preference into the static `$locale` field), making the home page look like the odd one out. Fix is a one-line `require_once __DIR__ . '/functions.php';` immediately before the i18n require in `waffle-menu.php` — guarantees `connectToDatabase` is defined whenever `initFromSession()` runs, so the DB preference lookup actually fires from every page that uses the shared header. Idempotent (`require_once`), and `functions.php` has no top-level side effects so loading it earlier is free. Same comment block explains the dependency so it doesn't get accidentally removed in a future cleanup. |

'/i18n.php'; I18n::initFromSession();` at the top of `includes/waffle-menu.php` itself — since that file is required by every module's header.php, **every page in the app now has i18n initialised for free** as a side-effect of using the shared header. Idempotent (safe to call again from pages that already init), single DB hit per page for the `interface_language` preference lookup, falls back gracefully to Accept-Language header then English if anything's missing. This also makes future i18n work cheaper: the shared header chrome now translates everywhere, and any module page that adds `t()` calls just works without needing its own init block. **Translation style**: Indic locales (hi, bn, ta, te, mr, kn, ml, gu, pa) rendered in native scripts (UTF-8, no escaping). Industry acronyms (ITSM, CMDB, LMS, SCORM, MFA) preserved as-is across all locales. Module names cross-checked for consistency with existing translations — e.g. fr "Calendrier" reused from the tickets module's existing translation so the same word appears on both the home tile and the in-app calendar nav. **"Service Desk"** rendered per locale convention (fr "Centre de services", es "Mesa de servicio", pt-BR "Central de Serviços", nl "Servicedesk", pl "Centrum obsługi", ru "Служба поддержки", de/it keep the English term per local convention, native scripts for Indic). **Out of scope (deferred to phase 1b)**: JS-rendered dynamic strings inside the MFA modal (`renderMfaContent()`, setup-step copy, toast messages from `showMfaMsg`/`showPwMsg`/`loadMfaBadge`) — those build their HTML/text in `waffle-menu.php`'s inline `<script>` block via string concatenation and stay English for now. The static modal scaffolding around them translates so the modals' titles, structural labels, and footer buttons display in the right language even though the dynamic content inside is still English. **Files touched**: `lang/en/common.php` (added 6 new top-level sections), `lang/<17 locales>/common.php` (mirror of the new sections, existing keys preserved verbatim), `index.php` (38 hardcoded strings → `t()` calls, plus i18n locale on `<html lang>`), `includes/waffle-menu.php` (i18n bootstrap at top, module-name `t()` lookups, waffle panel + user menu + modal labels all `t()`'d). |

Canvas overflow set to `hidden` in Present mode so the now-redundant scrollbars don't show. |
| 258 | Network Mapper    | Feature     | **Auto-centre tool** — one-click button that recentres every node so the diagram's bounding box sits centred on the selected paper size. New **Centre** button in the editor toolbar between Branding and PNG/PDF export. Computes the bbox of placed nodes including the label that hangs ~40px below each icon (so the optical centre matches the visual centre, not just the icon centre — labels would otherwise drag the perceived bottom edge of the diagram off), reads the page rectangle via the existing `pageDimensionsPx(diagram.paper_size, diagram.paper_orientation)` helper, computes the shift that lands the bbox centre on the page centre, snaps that delta to 20px (so the existing grid alignment is preserved across the whole diagram — snapping each node individually would risk breaking relative spacing), and applies it to every node's `x` / `y`. **Persistent**, not a visual transform — mutates node coordinates so the centring survives save/reload and is captured by PNG/PDF exports. Connectors auto-follow since `renderConnectors()` reads live node positions; brand strip + page outline are unaffected. **Validation toasts** for the failure modes: empty diagram ("Nothing to centre — place some nodes first"), no paper size set ("Set a page size first (Page dropdown)"), bbox bigger than the page ("Diagram is too large to centre on this page size — try a larger paper or use Fit + zoom" — bails rather than letting some nodes spill off-page silently), already centred (no-op toast). **Read-only versions**: button is hard-disabled via `applyReadOnlyState` with a "Historical versions are read-only" tooltip — more honest than letting the user click into a no-op.
