| 257 | Network Mapper    | Feature     | **PNG / PDF export of diagrams**. Two new toolbar buttons (segmented `PNG` / `PDF` group between Branding and Present) snapshot the diagram for sharing or printing. Capture is WYSIWYG with the page outline: if a paper size is set, the export clips exactly to the page rectangle (`pageDimensionsPx(diagram.paper_size, diagram.paper_orientation)`), otherwise it crops to the bounding box of placed nodes plus 40px padding. Branding header/footer, page outline, connectors, node icons, and labels all render in the output exactly as they appear on screen. **Implementation**: html2canvas 1.4.1 (~200 KB) for rasterisation + jsPDF 2.5.2 (~360 KB) for PDF wrapping, both vendored locally at `assets/js/vendor/` so the feature works offline. Eager-loaded from `diagram.php` since the editor is a heavy page already and lazy-loading adds complexity for marginal gain. **Capture flow**: stash current zoom + scroll + selection, clear the selected node/connector (so cyan rings/strokes don't bleed into the export), reset zoom to 1× so the rasteriser captures at native resolution, add `.is-exporting` class to `.nm-canvas-inner` (CSS hides edge handles, selection rings, the empty-state placeholder, and forces connectors to render with the default slate arrow regardless of selection), call `html2canvas(elCanvasInner, { x, y, width, height, scale: 2, backgroundColor: '#fff', useCORS: true })`, restore everything in a `finally` block so failures don't leave the editor stuck in capture mode. **Output**: PNG via `canvas.toDataURL('image/png')` + a synthetic `<a download>` click; PDF via `new jsPDF({ orientation, format: paperSize.toLowerCase() })` + `doc.addImage(...)` filling the page edge-to-edge. **Filename slugifies** the diagram title + version label so "Production Network" v2 exports as `production-network-v2.png` / `.pdf`. **Validation**: refuses to export an empty diagram with no paper size set (toast: "Nothing to export — place some nodes or set a page size first") so the user doesn't get a blank canvas file. Read-only versions can export too — it's a view-only operation, no `is_current` gating needed. **2× scale** chosen for crisp output on retina screens and when zoomed during a presentation; PDFs use the actual paper size + orientation so the file opens at the right physical dimensions for printing. Toast on success ("PNG exported" / "PDF exported"). |

| 256 | Network Mapper    | Feature     | **Zoom controls + Present mode**. Two complementary view features for the editor. **Zoom**: new 4-button segmented group in the editor toolbar (between Page and Branding) — `−` zooms out one step, the centre label shows the current level and click-resets to 100%, `+` zooms in one step, and **Fit** scales to fit the page outline (if a paper size is set) or the bounding box of all placed nodes (otherwise) into the visible canvas with 40px padding. F11 is intentionally left to the browser for true OS-fullscreen escalation, since synthesising a Fullscreen API call from JS requires user-gesture chaining and adds an extra approval prompt — the tooltip on Present spells out the F11 path so the user knows the sequence. Designed for screen-sharing review meetings: click Present → F11 → walk through the diagram → F11 to exit fullscreen → Esc to leave Present and resume editing. **Refactor**: changed all `elCanvas.appendChild`/`querySelectorAll` calls that target diagram children to use `elCanvasInner` instead, so child management and the zoom transform target the same element. `elCanvas` keeps its role as the scroll viewport (overflow:auto + getBoundingClientRect). | 255 | Network Mapper    | Fix         | **Header/footer strip silently skipped after opening the Branding modal**. Saving the per-diagram Branding modal with no input changes stamped six empty strings into the new `header_left`/`center`/`right` + `footer_left`/`center`/`right` columns. The render path treated `''` as an explicit "blank this slot" override (distinct from `NULL` = "inherit org default"), so the org-wide defaults were bypassed and — since all six resolved to empty — the strip-skip-when-all-empty short-circuit fired and the overlay never appeared. Two fixes: **(a)** the modal's commit handler in `assets/js/network-mapper.js` now writes `null` for any empty input (instead of `''`), so leaving a slot blank means "inherit" — which matches the modal's own UX where the placeholder text already shows the org default for context; **(b)** a one-off `UPDATE network_diagrams SET header_*/footer_* = NULL WHERE header_*/footer_* = ''` cleaned up any rows already poisoned by the trap. The "explicit blank override" semantics were lost in the process but they weren't exposed in the UI anyway — there was no affordance to set a slot to "explicitly empty" distinct from "use org default", so removing that distinction simplifies the mental model. Reset button continues to clear all six overrides back to NULL in one click. |

Picking a size renders a subtle dashed cyan outline on the canvas at the actual paper dimensions (computed at 96 DPI — A4 portrait 794×1123px, A3 landscape 1587×1123px, etc.) so analysts can compose diagrams inside the printable area before sharing/screenshotting/exporting. **Persisted per-diagram** via two new nullable columns on `network_diagrams` (`paper_size` VARCHAR(20), `paper_orientation` VARCHAR(20)) so reopening the diagram shows the same outline; **carried forward on save-as-new-version** so analysts don't have to re-pick on every version fork (added to `create_version.php`'s INSERT alongside the existing fields). Both columns NULL by default — existing diagrams render exactly as they did, no overlay shown until the user explicitly picks a size. Schema added in three places per the mandatory checklist: `database/freeitsm.sql` CREATE TABLE, `api/system/db_verify.php` schema map (so existing installs pick up the columns on next verify run via the auto-ALTER), and the API endpoints. **Server-side whitelist** on `save_diagram.php` for both fields (5 size values + 2 orientations) so the picker can't be coerced into storing junk that the JS doesn't know how to render. **Outline visuals**: SVG `<rect>` with `fill: white; opacity: 0.55` so the dot-grid bleeds through (visually distinguishes on-page from off-page area), plus a `stroke: #06b6d4; stroke-width: 1.5; stroke-dasharray: 8 5` border with cyan branding. Corner `<text>` label naming the chosen paper (e.g. "A3 landscape") so the user can tell at a glance which size is active without checking the toolbar. Outline is inserted as the SVG's second child (after `<defs>`) so it renders behind connectors but above the canvas background. **Toolbar button label updates live** to show the current pick — `Page: Off`, `Page: A4 L`, `Page: A3 P` etc. so the active state is visible without opening the dropdown. **Read-only versions**: the dropdown opens (so historical-version viewers can see what paper was chosen) but picking a different size is rejected with a toast since paper settings would be a mutation. Dropdown closes on Esc, outside-click, or re-press of the button — same pattern as the Versions dropdown. **Help screen** gets a new section 7 (Page size guide) explaining the workflow and previewing the upcoming PNG/PDF export feature that'll use these bounds. Single-page only for v1; multi-page tiling (draw.io-style) deferred. |
| 251 | Network Mapper    | Improvement | **Node labels no longer split mid-character** ("FREEITSM" was wrapping as "FREEIT / SM"). Root cause: `.nm-node-label` used `word-break: break-word` which aggressively breaks at any character to fit the 110px label width. Industry convention (Lucidchart, AWS architecture tools, draw.io) is to break at word boundaries first and only fall back to character breaks if a single token genuinely overflows. Fix: switched to `overflow-wrap: break-word` (lighter touch — only breaks single words when they'd literally overflow), widened the label cap from 110px → 140px so multi-word names like "Production Database" sit on one line more often, added `hyphens: auto` so the browser can break at hyphenation points if needed (useful for things like `prod-db-01.example.com`). Kept the 2-line clamp + ellipsis as the last-resort overflow handler so a really long name still gets bounded. Tooltip (`title` attr) on every label already showed the full name on hover — unchanged. Also added the standard `line-clamp` property next to `-webkit-line-clamp` to fix the pre-existing vendor-prefix lint warning that's been showing on every diagram.php edit since chunk B/C. Behaviour summary: "FREEITSM" → stays whole on one line. "Production Database Server" → wraps as `Production / Database Server`. "prod-db-01.example.com" → breaks at hyphens/dots, ellipsis if still too long. CSS-only change, no JS or schema touched. |
| 250 | Network Mapper    | Feature     | **CMDB properties shown in the node detail panel**. Selecting a node now lazy-fetches `get_object.php?id=<cmdb_object_id>` and renders every property that has a value into a new **Properties** section in the detail panel — `from CMDB` subtitle so it's clear where the data comes from. **Empty properties are filtered out** per Ed's explicit ask (don't show fields the user has left blank), with per-type emptiness rules so e.g. a number of zero or a boolean explicitly set to No still shows (only `null`/missing is treated as empty). **Type-aware rendering** mirrors the cmdb/object.php detail page conventions: **text** auto-detects HTTP/HTTPS URLs and linkifies them in cyan, plain strings render as-is; **number** uses `toLocaleString()` so big numbers get thousand separators; **date** parses ISO strings and uses `toLocaleDateString()` so it matches the rest of the app's date display; **boolean** shows a green "Yes" or grey "No" rather than raw true/false; **dropdown** renders as a coloured pill picking up the option's `colour` from cmdb_class_property_options (with a luminance heuristic to pick black or white text for legibility on dark backgrounds, matching how CMDB browse tables pick pill text colour); **object_ref** renders as a pink-pill link straight to `cmdb/object.php?id=X` in a new tab (same pink-pill aesthetic CMDB uses for object references, so the panel and CMDB feel like one app). Same flag is cleared in `closeDetail` so a slow fetch can't paint into a closed panel. **No new API endpoint** — reuses `api/cmdb/get_object.php` which already returns the full property bag (along with relationships, children, etc. that the panel just ignores). One round-trip per selection — cheap, and freshness wins over caching since CMDB values can change underneath the diagram between selections. | 244 | Network Mapper    | Feature     | **Chunk D Part 1 — connectors**. End result: place two new nodes, draw a connector between them, hit save → all three rows get real ids in a single round-trip. | 243 | Network Mapper    | Fix         | **`get_diagram.php` SQL error referencing non-existent `c.icon_key` column**. `cmdb_classes` holds an `icon_id` FK; the actual `icon_key` string lives on `cmdb_icons` (separate lookup table so renaming an icon doesn't require touching every class row that uses it). The query joined `cmdb_classes` but tried to `SELECT c.icon_key`, triggering `SQLSTATE[42S22]: Column not found: 1054 Unknown column 'c.icon_key' in 'field list'` — visible right next to the autosave indicator on initial diagram load because `loadDiagram()`'s catch surfaces the exception message into the status area. The mistake slipped through chunks A and B because chunk B's save flow didn't refetch on success — chunk C's "save then reload to resolve temp ids" path was the first thing to actually call `get_diagram` against a diagram with nodes. Fix is a one-line `LEFT JOIN cmdb_icons i ON i.id = c.icon_id` and switching the projection from `c.icon_key` to `i.icon_key`, matching the existing pattern in `get_classes.php`. LEFT (not INNER) so classes without an icon assignment still load — `class_icon` comes back null and the frontend falls back to the box default. |

| 240 | Network Mapper    | Feature     | **New module — Network Mapper, Chunk A (foundation)**. First slice of a new visual module for drawing network/architecture diagrams that sit on top of the CMDB. Versioning baked in from day one: each diagram is one row in a `network_diagrams` chain linked by `parent_diagram_id` — the leaf (no children) is the editable "current" version; older nodes are read-only history. New schema (`database/freeitsm.sql` + `db_verify.php`): **`network_diagrams`** (id, parent_diagram_id self-FK with ON DELETE SET NULL so deleting one version doesn't cascade, title, description, version_label, created_by_analyst_id, created/updated datetimes), **`network_diagram_nodes`** (diagram_id, cmdb_object_id binding, x/y position, size enum 'small/medium/large', icon_override for per-node visual swap), **`network_diagram_connectors`** (diagram_id, from/to node ids, optional cmdb_relationship_id link, label, line_style). FKs cascade nodes+connectors on diagram delete; node delete cascades its incident connectors. Seven backend endpoints under `api/network-mapper/`: `list_diagrams.php` (leaf versions only — uses `WHERE id NOT IN (SELECT parent_diagram_id…)` to filter to current versions, returns per-row node/connector counts plus a `version_count` walked across the chain), `list_versions.php` (root-to-leaf chain ordered oldest first, each flagged `is_current` if it has no children), `get_diagram.php` (single version hydrated — nodes carry CMDB object name + class + icon + `is_planned`, connectors include their CMDB relationship link), `create_diagram.php` (POST title/description/version_label, defaults to `v1`), `create_version.php` (clones nodes+connectors forward into a new diagram row chained to parent — builds a `nodeIdMap` so connector refs translate to the new node ids; refuses to fork an already-forked parent so no branching in v1), `save_diagram.php` (transactional delete+reinsert with temp→real node id mapping; refuses to save non-leaf versions, only updates metadata fields the caller explicitly sends so per-field inline edits don't clobber others), `delete_diagram.php` (single version delete — older versions in the chain preserved via the SET NULL parent_diagram_id behaviour). Module pages: `network-mapper/index.php` (diagrams landing — grid of cards each showing title, version pill, description preview, node/connector counts, author, updated date; filter-by-title; "+ New diagram" modal with title/description/initial version label; per-card delete with confirmation), `network-mapper/includes/header.php` (standard waffle-menu + module title + Diagrams nav button), `network-mapper/diagram.php` (Chunk A stub editor — title bar with version pill that goes amber+"read-only" for historical versions, metadata row, placeholder canvas + class palette; full drag-to-canvas / bind-to-CMDB / autosave lands in subsequent chunks). Module added to the waffle menu (between CMDB and System) and `module-colors.php` with cyan branding (`#06b6d4` → `#0891b2`, distinct from CMDB pink and Process Mapper indigo). |
| 239 | CMDB              | Feature     | **Planned objects** — record future-state architecture in the same CMDB as your real estate. New `is_planned` boolean column on `cmdb_objects` (default 0 = real, 1 = planned). Toggle exposed in the New Object modal (under the required-fields block, with explainer copy) and on the object detail page header (a checkbox next to Parent and Created/Updated, with "Yes (future state)" / "No (real, in service)" label). Planned status persists via `save_object.php` — caller can include `is_planned` in the payload to update it, or omit it to leave the existing value untouched (matches the inline-edit-one-field pattern used elsewhere so editing a property doesn't accidentally reset the flag). Round-trips through `get_object.php`, `get_objects.php`, and `search_objects.php` (the autocomplete picker that the upcoming Network Mapper will use). **Visual rendering**: amber **PLANNED** pill rendered next to the object name in the browse table + the object detail header, with a dashed border + soft amber background on the header card itself so the future-state distinction reads at a glance. Browse rows for planned objects get a subtle opacity reduction + italic name for the same reason. CSS uses the standard `fef3c7 / fcd34d / 92400e` amber triad. **AI summary** prompt taught to surface planned status near the start of the synthesis and frame the sentence in future tense ("will host…", "is proposed to…", "is a planned…") so the reader knows immediately the object isn't yet in service — turns the prose synthesis into an unambiguous as-is/to-be indicator. Schema migration via `db_verify.php` (single column add, default 0 = no data migration needed for existing rows). Foundation for the upcoming Network Mapper module's "draft architecture" use case but immediately useful in its own right for change-planning workflows and pre-migration CMDB modelling. |
| 238 | Tickets           | Feature     | **Tickets module i18n — phase 1a**. Second module pilot-converted to use the i18n layer after Process Mapper, across all 18 supported locales. Phase 1a scope = every PHP-rendered string users see on inbox page load: **header nav** (`Inbox` / `Dashboard` / `Users` / `Calendar` / `Rota` / `Settings` / `Help`); **folder panel** (`Folders` heading + `Department` / `Analyst` group toggle); **email list** (the dynamic `All Tickets` placeholder + the three icon-button tooltips for new / search / refresh); **reading pane** empty states; **five modals** (Add Note, Reply/Forward, Create New Ticket, Search Tickets, Schedule Work) including every label, placeholder, dropdown option, and button; the **AI Chat panel** (title, welcome text, input placeholder). About 70 translation keys added under `tickets.nav.*`, `tickets.folders.*`, `tickets.list.*`, `tickets.reading_pane.*`, `tickets.note_modal.*`, `tickets.reply_modal.*`, `tickets.new_ticket_modal.*`, `tickets.search_modal.*`, `tickets.schedule_modal.*`, and `tickets.ai_chat.*`. **All 18 languages updated** in parallel (en + fr/de/es/pt-BR/nl/it/pl/ru + hi/bn/ta/te/mr/kn/ml/gu/pa). The shared header uses `function_exists('t')` guards as a safety net so any unconverted page that includes it (calendar, rota, users, settings sub-pages, help) still renders English literals without breaking. `tickets/index.php` initialises i18n + emits `window.translations` for the `['common', 'tickets']` namespaces ready for the JS bridge. **Out of scope for phase 1a (deferred to phase 1b)**: dynamic strings rendered by the 2,771-line `inbox.js` (toasts, ticket card content, runtime-built column headers, notification messages, error toasts); ticket statuses and priorities that come from DB lookup tables (those translate via a different mechanism than `t()`); and the settings / dashboard / calendar / rota / users / help sub-pages. Two modules now fully i18n'd on their main screens. |

### 15 May 2026

| ID  | Module            | Type        | Description |
|-----|-------------------|-------------|-------------|
| 232 | Process Mapper    | Feature     | **Export to Mermaid** — new toolbar `Export` button (upload-arrow icon, next to Lane) opens a modal showing the current process as [Mermaid](https://mermaid.js.org/) flowchart markup, ready to paste into any Markdown surface that supports it (GitHub/GitLab READMEs + wikis, Notion, Confluence, Obsidian, Mermaid Live Editor). Generator details: `flowchart LR` direction so lanes-as-subgraphs stack vertically into proper horizontal swimlanes; one `subgraph laneN["Label"] ... end` block per lane in `display_order`, with steps placed inside their lane's block based on `lane_id`; unlaned steps emitted at top level. Step shapes use classic Mermaid syntax for maximum renderer compatibility: Process → `id["label"]`, Decision → `id{"label"}`, Terminal → `id(["label"])`, Document → `id[/"label"/]`. Node IDs derived from `step.id` (or `step.tempId` with `t` prefix and `Math.abs()` for new unsaved steps). Connectors become `-->` arrows, gaining `-->|"label"|` when labelled — Mermaid resolves IDs across subgraph boundaries so cross-lane connectors render naturally. Labels are HTML-entity-escaped (`&`, `"`, `<`, `>` → entities; `\n` → `<br/>`) so weird characters in step names don't break the markup. Modal has a textarea pre-selected on open (Ctrl-A → Ctrl-C works as a fallback for the Copy button, which uses the Clipboard API with a select-and-toast fallback if blocked). Hand-placed positions, colours, gradients, and groups deliberately not exported — Mermaid auto-layouts and only has subgraphs (already used for lanes). Lossy on visuals, faithful on structure. Purely frontend; no API or schema changes. |
| 231 | Process Mapper    | Fix         | **Lane divider drag now actually moves the contents below**. Previously the divider followed the cursor pixel-by-pixel but each per-frame `delta` (often 1px) got eaten by `snap()` when applied to step positions — `snap(200 + 1) = 200` — so contents never moved no matter how far the divider was dragged. The divider visually drifted away from anything below it, leaving items glued at their original `y`. Fix: snap `targetH` to the grid in the resize mousemove handler (`const targetH = Math.max(80, snap(laneDragging.startHeight + dy))`), so lane heights now change in 20px increments matching the step grid. With grid-aligned deltas, the shift in `resizeLaneTo` applies cleanly: contents move 20px each time the divider crosses a grid line. Drag feels "snappy" in the same way step drag already does — consistent across the whole UI. Detail panel's Height input intentionally left unsnapped so typed values are respected for fine-tuning. |
| 230 | Process Mapper    | Fix         | **Resizing a lane now physically moves everything below the divider** with it (lanes, steps, groups). Previously the resize shifted steps in lanes below based on `step.lane_id` matching, so any step with a missing or stale `lane_id` (e.g. one placed before its lane was tagged) would stay anchored at its old `y` while its lane band shifted underneath it — leaving the step "stranded" in the wrong lane and creating confusion about which lane it belonged to. Fix swaps the criterion from `lane_id` matching to **visual centre position vs the resized lane's bottom edge** (matching how groups already worked), so anything visually below the divider moves by the same delta the divider moved. Stale `lane_id` values are not re-tagged inside the resize — that's left to the existing auto-tag pass at the start of the next lane drag, which keeps the lane logic itself untouched. |
| 229 | Process Mapper    | Improvement | **Detail panel now survives autosave** — previously, every autosave call ran `openProcess()` after the response to refresh real IDs, and `openProcess()` unconditionally called `closeDetail()`. So if you were editing a step/group/lane's properties, the panel would slide closed every 2 seconds and you'd have to re-click the thing to keep going. Fix has two parts: (1) `openProcess()` gains a `preserveDetail` parameter; `save()` passes `true`, sidebar process-click still passes the default `false` so switching processes still closes the panel cleanly. (2) `save()` captures the current selection by **stable identity** (step's `{x, y}`, group's `{x, y, width, height}`, lane's `display_order`) *before* the save runs, then after `openProcess(newId, true)` reloads the data with fresh real IDs, re-finds the equivalent entity and calls `showDetailForStep/Group/Lane()` to re-populate the panel with the new IDs. Position-based matching is robust because positions are saved as part of the same payload, so the reloaded data has the same coords. If the entity can't be found after reload (e.g. it was deleted in the meantime), the panel closes gracefully. Multi-step selections (size > 1) aren't preserved — the panel only shows single-entity details anyway. |
| 228 | Process Mapper    | Fix         | **Group/step/lane drag occasionally snapped back mid-drag** because the autosave timer (2s after the last `markDirty`) could fire *during* a drag. `save()` calls `openProcess()` after the response lands to refresh real IDs, and that reload destroys the in-progress element and calls `closeDetail()` — so the user saw the panel slide closed and the group/step/lane revert to its last-committed size. Pure timing collision so it only manifested when a drag happened to start 1–2s after an earlier dirty edit. Fix: `scheduleAutosave()` now checks for any active drag state (`dragging`, `groupDragging`, `laneDragging`, `connectDrag`, `rubberBand`) when the timer fires; if a drag is in progress, the timer reschedules itself for another `AUTOSAVE_DEBOUNCE_MS` and re-checks — so save only fires once the mouse is released. Manual `Ctrl+S` mid-drag is still possible but a corner case; left unguarded to avoid surprising the user. |
| 227 | Process Mapper    | Feature     | **Groups now own their contents** — drag a group and the steps inside come with it. New nullable `group_id` column on `process_steps` (mirrors the `lane_id` pattern); `freeitsm.sql` + `db_verify.php` schemas updated with a matching `idx_ps_group` index. New `groupAtPoint(x, y)` helper returns the *smallest* group whose rectangle contains the point (smallest-wins disambiguates overlapping groups in favour of a nested inner one), and `autoAssignAllStepGroups()` runs at the start of every group drag to stamp `group_id` on each step from its current visual position — catches pre-existing steps that were never officially tagged. During a group's `move` drag, the move handler applies the per-frame `actualDx`/`actualDy` delta to every step where `step.group_id == groupDragging.id`, so contained steps track the group rigidly. On `mouseup` after a move, those carried steps run `reassignStepLanes()` since their absolute Y has changed; on `mouseup` after a resize, all steps re-run `autoAssignAllStepGroups()` since the group's bounds (and therefore membership) may have shifted. New steps created via `addStep()` pick up `group_id` from their drop position automatically. `reassignStepGroups(stepIds)` runs alongside `reassignStepLanes()` after every step drag-end so manual step movement updates membership. Group delete clears `group_id` on contained steps (matches lane delete behaviour — steps survive, position preserved). `api/process-mapper/save.php` now inserts groups *before* steps with a `groupIdMap[oldRef -> realId]` table; step inserts translate frontend `group_id` (real id or temp negative id) into the persisted group id, or NULL if unresolvable. Coexistence with lanes: a step can carry both `lane_id` and `group_id` independently — dragging a group brings its steps along, dragging a lane brings its steps along; the two never fire at the same time so they don't conflict. |
| 226 | Process Mapper    | Fix         | **Groups inside a lane now move with the lane** on reorder, resize, and delete. Original design said groups stay at their absolute position (no `lane_id` column — groups are deliberately free-form), but in practice if you draw a group around a sub-flow inside a lane you expect it to follow the lane like the steps do. Fix: each lane operation now snapshots groups' `yWithinLane` derived on the fly from each group's vertical centre (since there's no stored column), then reapplies positions after the lane stack reflows. `reorderLaneTo()` does this in the same snapshot/reorder/reapply pass as steps. `resizeLaneTo()` shifts groups in lanes below by the same delta as their lane's bandTop changed. `deleteSelectedLane()` shifts groups in lanes below up by the deleted lane's height. Groups that aren't visually inside any lane (e.g. floating in empty canvas) stay put — unchanged behaviour. No data model change needed; the lane derivation is purely runtime, so groups remain free-form and can still be moved across lane boundaries or out of lanes entirely. |
| 225 | Process Mapper    | Fix         | **Steps that visually sat inside a lane but had no `lane_id` got left behind when their lane was reordered or resized**. This bit anyone who added steps before adding lanes (the common case for existing diagrams) — the steps look like they belong to a lane but internally `lane_id` is still null, so `reorderLaneTo()` and `resizeLaneTo()` skip them. New `autoAssignAllStepLanes()` helper scans every step and stamps its `lane_id` based on whichever lane its vertical centre currently sits in; called at the start of every lane drag (header or divider) so the upcoming reorder/resize math operates on a fully-tagged step set. Idempotent and cheap. Also fixed a secondary arithmetic bug in the reorder-trigger loop: when iterating lanes to find which slot the cursor is over, the dragged lane's height was being skipped from the running `acc` because of an early-`continue`, so non-dragged lane midlines were computed without accounting for the dragged lane's still-occupied visual space. Result: the swap fired too eagerly (cursor only needed to cross y=90 instead of y=270 in a 2-lane test). Loop now accumulates `acc` unconditionally and only skips the *test* against the cursor when iterating the dragged lane itself. |
| 224 | Process Mapper    | Fix         | **Lanes were invisible after creation** because `.pm-canvas` had `position: relative` but no stacking-context root, so lanes at `z-index: -1` painted *behind* the canvas's own dot-grid background instead of between the background and the z>=0 children (groups, connectors, steps). Added `isolation: isolate` to `.pm-canvas` so it forms its own stacking context — now negative-z descendants paint in step 2 of the CSS painting order (after the canvas's background, before z>=0 children), which is exactly where lanes should sit. One-line fix, no JS changes. Spotted on first user click of the Lane toolbar button: the lane was being created and selected (label visible in the detail panel) but no band appeared on the canvas. |
| 223 | Process Mapper    | Feature     | **Swimlanes — full v1 with reorder + resize + step ownership**. Phase 2 of the grouping work, now landed. New toolbar **Lane** button drops a 180px-tall horizontal band at the bottom of the lane stack with a sensible default label ("Lane N"). Lanes render as full-width bands behind everything else (CSS `z-index: -1`, between the dot-grid background and groups at z=0). Each lane has a left-edge vertical header (50px wide, uppercase letter-spaced label) you click to select, and a 6px bottom edge you drag to resize. **Step ownership** via new nullable `lane_id` column on `process_steps`: every step-drag mouseup runs `reassignStepLanes()` which uses the step's vertical centre to figure out which lane band it's in and stamps `lane_id` accordingly (or `null` if outside every lane). `addStep()` does the same on creation so a step dropped on a new canvas position picks up its lane immediately. **Reorder via header drag**: drag the lane's left-edge header up/down and the lane snaps between slots as the cursor crosses each neighbour's midline; `reorderLaneTo()` captures every step's `yWithinLane` snapshot before the move, swaps display_order positions, recomputes lane bandTops, then reapplies each step's offset against its lane's new bandTop — so steps perfectly track their lane across the swap. **Resize via divider drag**: drag the lane's bottom edge to grow/shrink (min 80px); `resizeLaneTo()` shifts every step in lanes *below* the resized lane by the same delta so they stay anchored to their own bands. **Delete a lane**: contained steps lose `lane_id` (kept their position so the user doesn't lose work), lanes below shift up to close the gap, their steps follow, display_order renumbers. **Gradient fills** on lanes too via the same `color2` mechanic shared with steps and groups — toolbar Gradient checkbox + second swatch in the lane detail panel. Per-lane detail panel inputs (label, height, order, colour pair) all live-update the canvas and round-trip through autosave. New `process_lanes` table (id, process_id, label, color, color2, display_order, height) + index on process_id; `process_steps.lane_id` INT NULL + index on lane_id. Backend save flow: lanes inserted *before* steps with a `laneIdMap[oldRef -> realId]` table built up; step inserts translate frontend `lane_id` (either real id or temp negative id) into the persisted lane id, or NULL if unresolvable. `get.php` returns lanes ORDER BY display_order, wrapped in try/catch like groups for installs that haven't run db_verify since this shipped. Z-index ladder: lanes -1, groups 0, connectors 1, steps 2 — no other CSS bumped. Coexistence: lanes, groups, and steps all work together — a group can span lanes, a step can sit in a lane and inside a group, lanes carry only steps (not groups). |
| 222 | Process Mapper    | Feature     | **Gradient fills on steps and groups** as a small polish pass ahead of swimlanes (lanes will inherit it for free). Each shape and group can now render as a two-stop `linear-gradient(135deg, color, color2)` instead of a flat fill. New `color2 VARCHAR(20) NULL` column on `process_steps` and `process_groups` — null means solid (existing behaviour preserved for every row). Detail panel's Colour input grows an inline `Gradient` checkbox + second-colour swatch; ticking the box reveals the second picker and updates the canvas live, unticking it clears `color2` and reverts to solid. When you first tick the box on a shape that's never had a gradient, the second picker is pre-seeded with a 40-unit darker `shade()` of the primary colour so the gradient looks deliberate from the first click — but it's just a default, you can pick anything. New `fillStyle(color, color2)` helper centralises the CSS string so the same one-liner handles both render paths (`createStepEl` and `applyGroupStyle`). Border colour on groups still derives from the primary colour only, which keeps the outline crisp against both solid and gradient fills without per-stop calculations. Full round-trip through save.php / get.php (`SELECT *` already returns the new column). Phase 2 (swimlanes) will follow next. |
| 221 | Process Mapper    | Feature     | **Groups — labelled coloured rectangles as a visual underlay** behind steps and connectors. | 220 | Process Mapper    | Feature     | **Autosave toggle with Word-style live status indicator** in the toolbar. New `Autosave` switch sits between the status text and the manual Save button; when on, a debounced save fires ~2 seconds after the last edit (no wasted writes on an untouched diagram, no half-finished-drag captures). Status line cycles through `✓ Saved` / `Unsaved` / `Saving…` / `⚠ Save failed — retry`, with `Autosave off` shown when the toggle is off. `Saving…` is held visible for at least 400ms so it doesn't just flash on fast saves. | 219 | Process Mapper    | Fix         | **Delete / Backspace now actually deletes the selected step or connector**. The canvas (`#pmCanvas`) has `tabindex="0"` and a keydown listener bound to it, but clicking a step fired `onStepMouseDown` which calls `e.preventDefault()` — suppressing the browser's default focus shift and leaving focus on `<body>` (or whatever toolbar button was last clicked). Delete/Backspace events fired on `<body>`, which is the canvas's *ancestor*, so they never bubbled to the canvas listener. Fix: explicit `canvas.focus({ preventScroll: true })` in `onStepMouseDown`, `onCanvasMouseDown`, and `selectConnector` so any selection action also pulls keyboard focus onto the canvas. `.pm-canvas` already has `outline: none` so there's no focus-ring artefact. |
| 218 | System            | Improvement | **D001 annotates known-benign PHP notices instead of filtering them** so the reader can tell whether each captured warning indicates a real problem or expected noise. Previously the diagnostic silently suppressed three message patterns (`headers already sent`, `session has already been started`, `Cannot change session`) but PHP 8.4's actual session-already-active wording is `"Ignoring session_start() because a session is already active"`, which didn't match any filter and leaked through with no context. Replaced the silent filters with an `$explainers` lookup that keeps the notice visible verbatim then appends an arrow-indented one-liner explaining *why* it's expected (e.g. "Expected — D001 already started a session, so PHP skipped the import's redundant session_start() call. Not a problem."). Covers all four known-benign patterns. Unrecognised warnings are still surfaced normally — they're the ones that might actually matter. |
| 217 | System            | Improvement | **D001 redacts more sensitive fields** so the report is safer to paste back to support on a real install. `DB_USERNAME` now reported as `(value redacted, length=N)` instead of in plain text (it's half a credential). `redact_row()` — which already blanked `password_hash` and `totp_secret` — extended to also redact `username`, `email`, `full_name`, `display_name`, `preferred_name` in the per-table "first row" sample, each replaced with `[redacted N chars]` so length-related issues (empty or absurdly long values) are still visible. Team/department/ticket_type names left visible since they're load-bearing for diagnosing config issues and rarely contain personal PII — the user can eyeball the report before pasting. |
| 216 | System            | Fix         | **D001 diagnostic false positives in LIVE IMPORT ATTEMPT** — the live-import section was reporting failures even on healthy installs. Two root causes: (1) the error-handler severity map referenced `E_STRICT`, which is deprecated in PHP 8.4+, so every captured warning emitted a recursive DEPRECATED notice that fell through to the default handler and dumped raw `<br><b>Deprecated</b>` HTML into the captured response body — which then failed to parse as JSON; (2) the import script uses relative `require_once '../../config.php'` resolved against CWD, and Apache sets CWD to the script's directory when serving it directly, but `include`-ing it from D001 leaves CWD as D001's directory so the path resolves one folder shy of the app root and `Failed opening required '../../config.php'` was reported. Fix: removed `E_STRICT` from the severity lookup (added a broader handful of stable constants instead, all comment-documented), and now `chdir(dirname($importPath))` before the include then restore CWD after so the relative includes resolve correctly. D001 now reports a clean run on a working install. |
| 215 | System            | Feature     | **Debug Tools library** at `system/debug-tools/` — app-store-style catalogue of self-contained diagnostics support can ask remote users to run when something fails. Each diagnostic is a single PHP file at `api/system/debug-tools/Dnnn_*.php` that emits a plain-text section-delimited report; the landing page lists each one with an ID badge, category tag, "when to run" description, the full list of checks, runtime, and side-effect notes, plus **Run** / **Copy** buttons that fetch the report into a dark code panel for one-shot copy-paste back to support. First diagnostic shipped: **D001 — Demo Core Data Import**, a 9-section report covering environment (PHP version, OS, extensions, memory/post limits), config files (`config.php`, `db_config.php`, DB constants), required files (import script, `core.json`, functions.php), JSON parse + record counts per table, DB connection (server version, charset, collation), per-table schema sanity for all 9 core tables (expected vs actual columns, row counts, redacted sample row), a transactional write probe (sentinel insert into each table inside a rolled-back transaction so we exercise write paths without persisting), and a live import attempt that includes the real `import_demo_data.php` in-process with a custom error handler capturing PHP warnings, then reports the full response + post-import row counts. Designed so the diagnostic itself never crashes — every section wrapped in try/catch, expected-column lists carried inline so it works even if `db_verify.php` is missing/broken, auth gate returns early with a clear message if not logged in. Wired into the system landing card grid and the system header nav. |

| 197 | CMDB              | Fix         | **Inline-edit a non-required property no longer fails with "Required property missing"** when some other required property is also set on the object. The save_object.php required-property validation was checking the request payload only — so editing e.g. *Email Address* on a Person sent only that one property in the payload, and the validator wrongly concluded *Employee Type* was missing (even though it was already saved on the row). Validation now skips required-property checks for fields the caller isn't explicitly touching: required is enforced on create (initial property values must be non-empty) and on update only when the caller explicitly sets a required property to empty. The common inline-edit-one-field case leaves untouched fields alone, matching how partial updates should work |

| 191 | CMDB              | Feature     | Add **AI Suggest Properties** to the CMDB Properties manager — the first v1 AI feature for the new module. A new **✨ Suggest with AI** button next to "Add Property" opens a two-stage wizard tailored to whatever class the analyst is editing. **Stage 1 (clarifying questions):** Claude is given the class name + description + any properties already defined, and returns 3-5 short questions about the analyst's specific environment (e.g. for *Database*: "What kind of database — SQL Server / Postgres / MongoDB / Redis?", "Do you track schemas separately?"). The prompt explicitly tells the AI that organisations run very different stacks so generic suggestions are useless without context, and to never ask whether a property is wanted — only about the environment. **Stage 2 (suggestions):** the answers are sent back along with the class context, and Claude returns 6-12 property suggestions, each with label / immutable property_key / type (text / number / date / boolean / dropdown / object_ref) / required-flag / one-line "why" rationale. Dropdown suggestions include a generated options list (3-8 typical values per the analyst's answers); object_ref suggestions include a target-class hint. The analyst sees a checked-by-default list (with the AI's reasoning visible inline beside each), unticks anything unwanted, and clicks **Add Selected** — properties are bulk-created via the existing `save_class_property.php` endpoint with full server-side validation. object_ref suggestions are flagged as "add manually" so the analyst picks the actual target class. The importer adds `process-mapper` to its allowed-modules list, and the demo-data page picks up a new module card and includes `process-mapper` in the post-core enable list |
| 170 | Process Mapper    | Feature     | Add a **help guide** for the Process Mapper module at `process-mapper/help.php`, fixing a dead link in the module header that pointed at a missing page. Styled to match the other module help guides (Forms, Tickets, Knowledge, etc.) with a left-pane navigation and seven scroll-spy sections — Overview (with feature cards and a four-step flow diagram), Creating a process, Step types (mini SVG previews of process / decision / terminal / document with their conventional uses and dimensions), Drawing connectors (edge-handle drag and Connect-tool modes, plus inline labels), Arranging & editing (drag, multi-select, Ctrl+A, arrow-key nudge, detail panel, delete), Saving & loading (Ctrl+S, sidebar list, search, delete), and Quick tips. Hero gradient and accents use the module's existing indigo brand (#6366f1 → #4338ca). All keyboard shortcuts rendered as styled `<kbd>` chips |
| 171 | Multiple Modules  | Improvement | **Cross-module lookup-table normalisation.** A pattern repeated throughout the codebase: a status / priority / type / impact column stored as a free-text VARCHAR with a hardcoded enum baked into PHP — adding a new value meant a code change. This release migrates five such columns into proper lookup tables sharing the same shape (id, name, colour, is_default, is_active, display_order, plus the relevant flag like is_closed or severity_order). **Tickets** — `tickets.status` & `priority` normalised into `ticket_statuses` (with `is_closed`) and `ticket_priorities`; rota's `ticket_rota_entries.location` normalised into `rota_locations` (Office, WFH); requester_email/name replaced with `users.user_id` FK. **Change Management** — `changes.change_type` / `status` / `priority` / `impact` (and the matching three on `change_templates`) normalised into four lookups; `change_statuses.is_closed` replaces literal-matching `'Completed'`. **Tasks** — `tasks.status` & `priority` normalised (with `is_closed` driving completed_datetime + open-task counters instead of literal-matching `'Done'` / `'Cancelled'`). **Service Status** — `status_incidents.status` normalised (with `is_resolved`) and `status_incident_services.impact_level` normalised (with `severity_order` replacing a hardcoded `ORDER BY CASE WHEN impact_level = 'Major Outage' THEN 1...` block in three different files). `db_verify.php` migrates each one in place — creates the lookup, seeds defaults, backfills ids from the legacy text (auto-creating any unrecognised values as new lookup rows so nothing is lost), adds the FKs and indexes, and only drops the legacy column once 100% of rows have migrated; pending rows are reported instead of forcing the drop. About 30 new endpoints across the five lookups follow the same hex-validated, only-one-default, refuse-delete-if-in-use pattern. Watchtower's stale literal-match filters all replaced with proper lookup joins. Calendar / dashboard hardcoded status→colour maps replaced with lookup-row colour values |
| 172 | Tickets           | Feature     | Add **Statuses** and **Priorities** tabs to **Tickets → Settings** so analysts can manage the new lookup tables without touching the database. Each tab follows the existing settings-page pattern (header, Add button, table with name / colour swatch / flags / order / active / actions). The shared edit modal grows three optional fields shown only when editing a status or priority — a colour picker (used for badges in lists, dashboards, watchtower), an "Is default" flag (auto-assigned to new tickets — the save endpoint clears the flag on every other row when one is set, and re-promotes the lowest-order row if no default remains), and a "Counts as closed" flag for statuses (drives `is_closed` so reports/queries can branch on the flag instead of literal-matching `'Closed'`). Six new endpoints under `api/tickets/`: `get_ticket_statuses.php`, `save_ticket_status.php`, `delete_ticket_status.php` and the priority equivalents — all session-gated, hex-colour-validated, and the deletes refuse with a friendly "X tickets currently use this — reassign first" message rather than letting the FK constraint surface a raw SQL error. The default row also can't be deleted. Save also refuses to deactivate a status (set `is_active = 0`) while any ticket still uses it, returning a friendly *"Cannot deactivate: N ticket(s) currently use this status"* error rather than letting the row disappear from the folder UI and leaving its tickets in limbo |
| 177 | Tickets           | Feature     | Add **drag-and-drop ticket triage** to the inbox. Drag any ticket from the email list onto a folder in the left pane to update it: drop on a Department folder reassigns the ticket to that department (status untouched), drop on a Department → Status subfolder updates both department and status in one go, drop on **Unassigned** clears the department. Status subfolders are now always rendered when a department is expanded (zero-count statuses appear with a dimmed badge) so any status is reachable as a drop target. Hovering a collapsed department for ~600 ms during a drag auto-expands it (Outlook-style spring-loaded folders) without changing the active view, and the subfolder group expand/collapse is now smoothly animated with a 200 ms grid-row transition (fixed by replacing full DOM rebuilds in `toggleFolder()` with targeted class flips on the existing nodes — the previous version was destroying and recreating the `.subfolder-group` element so the CSS transition had nothing to animate from). Drop targets get a blue dashed outline during drag-over, and the dragged email row goes semi-transparent. Reuses the existing `api/tickets/assign_ticket.php` endpoint, so the `closed_datetime` stamp and the `ticket_closed` template-email trigger all fire for free when a ticket is dragged onto a closed status. After a successful drop the folder counts and email list refresh, the reading-pane (right) properties panel refreshes if it was showing the dropped ticket, audit history is written for whichever fields actually changed, and a toast confirms the move |
| 183 | Multiple Modules  | Improvement | **Make ticket statuses drive every UI surface.** Once the lookup table existed, the rest of the codebase still had several places that hardcoded `['Open', 'In Progress', 'On Hold', 'Closed']` — meaning the seeded `Awaiting Response` status existed in the database but was invisible in the UI. This release sweeps those out: the **inbox folder pane** (`get_ticket_counts.php` now returns the dynamic `statuses[]` master list and the frontend iterates it; subfolder click moved off inline `onclick` to a delegated listener so status names with apostrophes don't break the page), the **reading-pane Status dropdown** (`displayEmail()` builds options from the lookup), the **analyst-side dashboard** widget filter (`tickets/dashboard/index.php` fetches `get_ticket_statuses.php` at init), the **self-service portal** summary cards (`api/self-service/get_dashboard.php` returns `ticket_summary.statuses[]` with name+colour+is_closed+count; the page renders one card per active non-closed status plus a Total card), the **self-service ticket-detail badge** (uses inline style derived from lookup `colour`), the **self-service recent-tickets table**, and the **Users-page tickets list**. Self-service drops its hardcoded `.status-open` / `.status-in-progress` / `.status-on-hold` / `.status-closed` CSS classes in favour of inline tinted-bg styles derived from each lookup row's `colour` field, so any new status added in settings styles itself correctly with no per-status CSS edit. Inactive statuses are excluded from all these surfaces. The seeded `Awaiting Response` status now appears as its own dashboard card, dropdown option and properly-coloured badge instead of being silently dropped or falling back to Open's colour scheme |
| 186 | Tickets           | Fix         | Render the status badge correctly on the **Users → user tickets** page (`tickets/users.php`). The badge class was built with `status-${status.toLowerCase()}` and matched against five hardcoded CSS rules (`.status-new`, `.status-open`, `.status-pending`, `.status-resolved`, `.status-closed`) — three of which referenced status names that aren't in the lookup at all (`new`, `pending`, `resolved`), and any seeded status containing a space (`In Progress`, `On Hold`, `Awaiting Response`) generated an invalid two-token class so the badge rendered uncoloured. `api/tickets/get_user_tickets.php` now joins `ts.colour AS status_colour`, the page renders the badge with an inline tinted-background + matching-colour-text style derived from the lookup, and the five dead `.status-*` CSS rules are removed |
| 187 | Tickets           | Improvement | Replace the three text buttons (`+ New`, `Search`, `Refresh`) above the inbox email list with compact 32×32 icon-only buttons (plus / magnifying-glass / refresh-arrow SVGs) and add `title` + `aria-label` tooltips for hover-discovery and screen readers. The "New" icon keeps a subtle green accent so it still reads as the create-action. The three legacy `.new-btn` / `.search-btn` / `.refresh-btn` CSS rules are replaced by a single shared `.icon-btn` style with a `.icon-btn-new` modifier for the green accent |
| 188 | Tickets           | Feature     | Add **AI Reply Cleanup** to the ticket compose modal. When an analyst hits Reply and types a rough draft (e.g. `"fixed it, restart machine"` or `"cost is £250 - ok?"`), a new **✨ Cleanup** button next to Send rewrites it via streaming Claude as a properly formatted email — `Dear [requester first name],`, paragraph breaks, grammar fixed, configured tone applied (Friendly / Formal / Brief), `Kind regards,` sign-off. The system prompt is locked down with explicit do/don't rules, four positive examples (substantial / technical-issue / hardware-request / account-access) and a no-padding negative example so Claude can't invent technical details, fabricate apologies, or pad the content; it turns fragments into proper sentences without becoming verbose. Context-aware: when a draft is fewer than ~15 words and has no full sentence, the endpoint pulls the ticket subject and first inbound email body, and the prompt adds one short context sentence + a verification ask phrased to fit the situation (test / try logging in / launch / confirm receipt — never the literal phrase "re-test" for delivered hardware, so a "new mouse" ticket gets `"please confirm it's set up correctly"` rather than asking the user to test the mouse). Streams live into TinyMCE via SSE — text chunks are buffered, formatted into HTML, and `setContent`'d on each chunk. An Undo link appears below the editor for 30 s after streaming completes (with a live countdown) and restores the original draft via `setContent` if clicked. New **Tickets → Settings → Reply Cleanup** tab houses a masked API-key input, model dropdown (Haiku 4.5 default, Sonnet 4.6, Opus 4.7), tone dropdown, **Test connection** button (1-token validation), a Custom Instructions textarea (max 4000 chars, persisted in `system_settings.tickets_reply_cleanup_custom_instructions` plain text, appended to the system prompt at runtime under a dedicated heading AFTER the safety scaffold so user-supplied rules can't override the anti-hallucination guards), and a collapsible "View system prompt" panel showing the full prompt with the greeting name as a `[requester first name]` placeholder and the tone clause filled in based on the currently-selected tone (re-fetches when the tone dropdown changes). The new Anthropic key (`tickets_reply_cleanup_api_key`) is registered in `ENCRYPTED_SETTING_KEYS` + `MASKED_SETTING_KEYS` and stored encrypted at rest; deliberately separate from the RFP AI / Knowledge AI / Forms AI keys so each feature has its own Anthropic workspace key for granular per-feature billing visibility on the Anthropic console. The system prompt is extracted into `includes/reply_cleanup_prompt.php` (`buildReplyCleanupSystemPrompt(...)`) so the runtime endpoint and the settings preview render from a single source of truth. Reuses the existing `rfpAiCallAnthropicStreaming` helper after a small backwards-compatible refactor — it now takes an optional `$settingsOverride` 4th argument so this feature can pass its own provider/key/model/verify-ssl dict instead of always reading the RFP AI defaults. New endpoints: `api/tickets/get_reply_cleanup_settings.php` (returns masked key + model + tone + custom instructions + prompt preview), `api/tickets/save_reply_cleanup_settings.php` (encrypts key on save, honours masked-no-change pattern), `api/tickets/test_reply_cleanup_key.php`, `api/tickets/ai_cleanup_reply.php` (SSE streaming endpoint). Cleanup button only shows in Reply mode (not Forward / New). Empty drafts and missing keys show friendly toasts. Audit history written for the original draft + cleaned version. Includes a deep-dive article at `freeitsm.co.uk/deep-dive/ai-reply-cleanup/` |

Useful when the style guide changes after generation, when a section has been heavily edited, or just for a polish pass. Available on both category sections (Restyle button alongside Edit/Re-generate/History) and framing sections (alongside Edit/Re-generate). Streams the response via the same SSE batch modal as generation, with a purple "Restyle —" prefix on the task row to distinguish from a generate. Snapshots current content into `rfp_section_history` before overwriting (category sections only — framing has no history table; the generate-from-scratch path is the recovery route). New `rfpAiRestyleStreaming()` helper, `restyle_section.php` and `restyle_framing.php` SSE endpoints |
| 148 | RFP Builder       | Feature     | Add invited suppliers page (Phase 5 step 5a) at `/contracts/rfp-builder/suppliers.php`. List of suppliers being evaluated for the RFP with their demo dates and notes (autosave on edit), Remove button on each row, "+ Invite supplier" button at the top opening a two-tab modal: "Pick existing" (datalist over the existing FreeITSM suppliers excluding any already invited to this RFP) or "Create prospective" (inline form for legal name + optional trading name + comments, creates a new supplier row tagged with the Prospective status if that lookup exists, then immediately invites them). Removing a supplier also clears any scores submitted against them on this RFP. The Phase 5 tile on the RFP overview now lights up automatically once consolidation is locked |
| 149 | RFP Builder       | Feature     | Add scoring page (Phase 5 step 5b) at `/contracts/rfp-builder/scoring.php`. Score one supplier at a time against every consolidated requirement, autosave on every score / notes change. Scoring scale 0-5 ("Does not meet" through "Excellent") plus an explicit "Not scored" option. Per-row notes for evidence and caveats. Sidebar lists every supplier on the RFP for one-click switching. Each requirement shows a pill summary of the team's other-analyst average if any (single-blind — count and average only, no names). Sticky bottom bar shows my running overall, scored count, and the team aggregate. Per-category averages live-update as you score. New `get_scores.php` endpoint returns requirements + my scores + others' aggregate, `save_score.php` upserts a single (analyst, supplier, requirement) score |
| 150 | RFP Builder       | Improvement | Rename "Invite supplier" UI throughout to "+ Add supplier" / "Add" / "Suppliers" since the system never actually sends invitations to suppliers — it's a purely internal record of who's being evaluated, with the PDF preview shared out-of-band. Schema and API endpoint names (`rfp_invited_suppliers`, `invite_supplier.php` etc) stay unchanged — they're internal names where "invited" remains a reasonable description of the link table semantics. New "Score" button on each supplier row links straight to the scoring page for that supplier |
| 151 | RFP Builder       | Improvement | Redesign the scoring page UX. Six click-to-light score boxes (0-5) per requirement with a red→green colour gradient (red 0, orange 1, yellow 2, lime 3, green 4, deep green 5); click again to clear. Notes textarea now spans the full row width and is twice the height. Left sidebar gains a live "Score by category" panel — every category lists its running average and X/Y scored count, click to scroll the main pane to that category. Sticky bottom bar gains a Spider button that opens a full-screen radar chart (Chart.js) showing per-category averages, with my scores in amber and other analysts' aggregate as a dashed purple overlay if any |
| 152 | RFP Builder       | Feature     | Add cross-supplier compare page (Phase 6 step 6a) at `/contracts/rfp-builder/compare.php`. Three-section side-by-side decision-making view: big-number cards for each supplier ranked by overall score (gold/silver/bronze ribbons for top three), multi-supplier radar chart overlaying every scored supplier on one set of category spokes (each in their own colour), and a category winners table marking the leading supplier per category with the gap to second place. New `get_compare_data.php` endpoint computes the multi-analyst rollup the same way as the per-supplier scoring page — mean across analysts per requirement, then mean of those across the requirements in each category, then mean of those across categories for the overall. Phase 6 tile on the RFP overview lights up as soon as any suppliers have been added |

Stats strip across the top: total consolidated, multi-dept categories, single-source categories, no-dept-linkage. Per-category and per-department row/column totals. One consolidated requirement counts in every department it has a source from. Linked from the consolidate page header once any consolidation data exists |
